The Five Legal Rulings of Basmalah
Enumerates the five rulings of basmalah with context

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five rulings of basmalah (wajib, sunnah, mubah, haram, makruh), identify the correct ruling for a given context, and explain why basmalah is not wajib in every situation according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Basmalah's ruling changes by context: wajib only if considered a verse of al-Fatiha, otherwise sunnah, mubah, haram, or makruh depending on the act.

The basmalah ('Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim') is a phrase of immense blessing, but the law does not treat it uniformly. Depending on where and how it is said, the ruling can range from obligatory to forbidden. This lesson walks through the five possible rulings as enumerated in the classical texts, clarifying the Hanafi position and the reasoning behind each classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five rulings
Read the passage and list the five rulings: wajib, sunnah, mubah, haram, makruh. Note the context given for each.
The passage also mentions an exception: basmalah in a sinful act with istihlal may lead to kufr.
2
Understand the wajib ruling
Note that basmalah is wajib only 'on the view that it is a verse of al-Fatiha' – the passage says this is against the Hanafi school (khilaf al-madhhab). The Hanafi position is that basmalah is not a verse of al-Fatiha, so the wajib ruling is not accepted.
The mention of 'khilaf al-madhhab' is key: this is a minority view within the school.
3
Analyze the sunnah and mubah contexts
Sunnah: at the start of wudu, eating, intercourse, and every important matter. Mubah: at the start of walking, sitting, and reciting al-Fatiha and surah in prayer (according to the preponderant view). The distinction is based on whether the act has inherent dignity.
The mubah category includes reciting basmalah before al-Fatiha; the Hanafi school holds it is not obligatory but permissible.
4
Examine the haram context
Basmalah is haram when said during prohibited acts: adultery, intercourse with a menstruating woman, drinking wine, eating usurped food without permission. The passage clarifies the ruling on kufr if one considers such acts lawful (istihlal).
The example of the stolen sheep from al-Durr al-Mukhtar illustrates a practical branch.
5
Review the makruh context
Basmalah is makruh at the beginning of Surah Bara'ah (Tawbah) and when engaging in doubtful matters (shubhat), including smoking and in places of impurity. During Surah Bara'ah, it is recommended to recite it within the surah, not at the start.
The ruling is from the Hanafi school; other schools may differ.

باسم الله تعالى لأنهما ليسا من أسمائه تعالى أجيب عن الثاني بأن التصدير باسم الله تعالى إما أن يكون بذكر اسم خاص، كلفظ الله مثلاً، أو بذكر اسم عام كلفظ اسم مضاف إليه تعالى، فإنه يراد به جميع أسمائه تعالى لعموم الإضافة، ويستفاد منه التبرك بالجميع وهو أولى وعن الأول بأن الباء من تتمة ذكره على الوجه المطلوب، قال القطب عبد القادر الجيلاني: الإسم الأعظم هو بشرط أن تقول الله وليس في قلبك سواه كذا في وقيل بينهما فرق فالرحمن أبلغ من الرحيم، إما بحسب شمول الرحمن للدارين، واختصاص الرحيم بالآخرة فإنه المعافي، والعفو يختص بالمؤمنين في الآخرة ويؤيده حديث الرحمة المسلسل بالأولية، وإما باعتبار جلائل خطبة الكتاب
على الأول من حيث الحكم، وعلى الثاني من حيث الكيف، وقيل فعلان لمبالغة الفعل، فيفيد جلالة الفعل وفعيل لمبالغة الفاعل فيفيد التكرار مرة بعد أخرى ففي كل منهما مبالغة ليست في الآخر (تتمة) ورد في الحديث : (إن الله خلق يوم خلق السموات والأرض مائة رحمة كل رحمة طباق ما بين السماء والأرض فجعل في الأرض منها واحدة فيها تعطف الوالدة على ولدها، والوحوش والطيور بعضها على بعض، وأخر تسعاً وتسعين، فإذا كان . القيامة أكملها بهذه يوم الرحمة) رواه أحمد وروى البخاري في كتاب التوحيد من صحيحه عن أبي هريرة فيما يرويه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن ربه عز وجل: إن رحمتي سبقت غضبي وفي رواية تغلب غضبي، والمراد بيان سعة الرحمة وشمولها للخلق حتى كأنها السابق والغالب، كما في شرح المشكاة، والمراد السبق والغلبة بإعتبار التعلق أي تعلق الرحمة غالب على تعلق الغضب لأن الرحمة مقتضى ذاته المقدسة والغضب متوقف على صدور ذنب من العبد
The Sermon of the Book. It is between... the station of remembrance for inability, and sometimes it is obligatory on the view that it is a verse of al-Fatiha, although it is against the school because the reports in it with constancy indicate obligation. And sometimes it is sunnah as in wudu, and at the beginning of every matter of significance including eating, intercourse, and the like. And sometimes it is permissible as in the Fatiha and surah according to the preponderant view, and at the beginning of walking and sitting for example, because it is sought for that which has honor, to safeguard against associating His name with trivial matters and to facilitate for the servants. So if one does it in trivial matters like wearing sandals with the intention of veneration and blessing, it is good. And sometimes it is forbidden as during adultery and intercourse with a menstruating woman, drinking wine, eating usurped or stolen food without seeking lawful permission or paying compensation. The correct is that if one considers that lawful during sin he disbelieves, otherwise not, and repentance is obligatory unless it is in a manner of disrespect, then he disbelieves as well. Among the branches on the weak view is what is at the end of the Book of Hunting from al-Durr al-Mukhtar: that if a thief slaughters a stolen sheep, and its owner finds it, it is not eaten due to the disbelief of the thief by his saying the name over a absolutely forbidden thing without ownership or legal permission. And know that the one who considers lawful does not disbelieve unless the forbidden is forbidden in itself and its prohibition is established by a definitive proof, otherwise not, as stated in al-Durar from al-Fatawa at the end of Kitab al-Khatr. So this sheep should be eaten, and it is supported by their statement that sacrifice with a usurped sheep is valid, but it is not permissible for him to eat or benefit according to the mufta bihi, even if he owns it before paying compensation or the owner's consent to payment or his acquittal or the judge's guarantee, because permissibility is another matter besides ownership. And sometimes it is makruh as at the beginning of Surah Bara'ah but not during it, so it is recommended. And when engaging in doubtful matters, and from it is when smoking tobacco, and in places of impurities. For if it is said: the beginning with the ba and the word ism is not beginning with the name of Allah because they are not from His names, it is answered regarding the second that prefacing with the name of Allah is either by mentioning a specific name like the word Allah, or by mentioning a general name like the word ism added to Him, then it is intended for all His names due to the generality of the addition, and blessing is derived from all, and that is better. And regarding the first, the ba is part of His remembrance in the desired manner. Al-Qutb Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani said: The Greatest Name is that you say Allah while there is nothing in your heart but Him, as in Sharh al-Mishkat. And al-Rahman al-Rahim: both are similar built for hyperbole, i.e., they indicate that it is by substance and usage, not by form and coinage, because forms of hyperbole are limited to the famous five, and among them is fa'il on condition that it is transitive and Rahim here is not transitive, and on condition that it is transformed from a subject. Therefore they said that Karim and Dharif are not from them because they are not transformed. And there is disagreement on al-Rahman and al-Rahim: are they synonymous like nadman and nadim, one mentioned after the other for emphasis? It is said yes, and it is said there is a difference, so al-Rahman is more comprehensive than al-Rahim, either by considering that al-Rahman encompasses both worlds and al-Rahim is specific to the Hereafter, for He is the Pardoner, and pardon is specific to the believers in the Hereafter, supported by the hadith of mercy with the chain of priority, or by considering major and minute blessings. So the hyperbole is in the first regarding the ruling, and in the second regarding the quality. And it is said that fa'lan is for hyperbole of the action, so it indicates majesty of the action, and fa'il is for hyperbole of the subject, so it indicates repetition time after time; thus each has a hyperbole not in the other. (Supplement) and it is reported in the hadith: 'Indeed Allah created on the day He created the heavens and the earth one hundred mercies, each mercy like the space between heaven and earth. He placed on earth one of them, in which a mother shows affection to her child, and wild animals and birds to each other, and withheld ninety-nine. So when the Day of Judgment comes, He completes them with this one, the day of mercy.' Narrated by Ahmad. And al-Bukhari narrated in Kitab al-Tawhid of his Sahih from Abu Hurayra relating from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) from his Lord: 'My mercy preceded My wrath' and in another narration 'overcomes My wrath.' The intent is to show the vastness of mercy and its encompassing of creation until it is as if it is the preceding and overwhelming, as in Sharh al-Mishkat. And what is meant is precedence and overcoming with regard to attachment, i.e., the attachment of mercy is dominant over the attachment of wrath because mercy is a requirement of His sacred essence, and wrath depends on the occurrence of a sin from the servant.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is from the opening sermon (khutbah) of the book, where the author discusses the legal rulings of saying Bismillah. The commentary first notes that basmalah can be wajib (obligatory) if one holds it is a verse of al-Fatiha, though this view is against the Hanafi school. The Hanafi position is that basmalah is not a verse of al-Fatiha, but the reports of the Prophet's constancy in reciting it indicate obligation in some contexts. Then it enumerates other rulings: sunnah (as in wudu and starting any important matter), mubah (permissible, e.g., before reciting Fatiha and surah according to the preponderant view), haram (forbidden, if used in sinful acts like adultery, drinking wine, etc.), and makruh (disliked, e.g., at the beginning of Surah Bara'ah). The passage also delves into the meaning of al-Rahman and al-Rahim, explaining their hyperbole forms and the famous hadith qudsi about mercy preceding wrath. The discussion of the sheep stolen and slaughtered is an illustrative branch from al-Durr al-Mukhtar on the ruling of eating such meat. The key point is that the ruling of basmalah varies with context, and one must be mindful of when it is appropriate or inappropriate.

Key Terms
البسملة (al-basmala): The act of saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'.
المواظبة (al-muwazabah): The Prophet's constancy in performing an act, which in Hanafi usul indicates sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
الاستحلال (al-istihlal): Considering a prohibited act to be lawful. In the passage, it is a condition for takfir when saying basmalah during sin.
الحرام لعينه (al-haram li-aynihi): An act that is prohibited in its very essence, such as zina, wine, and theft, as opposed to acts that are prohibited due to an external factor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of saying 'Bismillah' before eating?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Mubah
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Basmalah is not always sunnah; it is haram when said during sins and makruh in certain contexts, while its recitation before al-Fatiha in prayer is mubah or sunnah, not wajib, according to the Hanafi school.

Hanafi Rulings on Salat and Salam upon the Prophet
Critical refinement of rulings and definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salat (fard once in a lifetime) and salam (not wajib), explain the definition of 'al' and 'sahabi', and distinguish the Hanafi position from al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Salat upon the Prophet is fard once in a lifetime; salam is not obligatory—a key Hanafi distinction.

Sending blessings and salutations upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) is a beloved act of worship, but its legal status varies. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi school's precise rulings: when salat is obligatory, when it is recommended, and how salam is viewed differently. We also clarify who is included in 'al' and 'sahabi', drawing on the commentary of al-Tahtawi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the hukm (legal ruling) for salat and salam separately. According to Hanafi school, salat is fard once in a lifetime, sunnah in tashahhud, and recommended otherwise. Salam is not wajib.
The text explicitly states that salat is fard once in a lifetime and that salam is not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the proofs cited: the hadith about how to send blessings (including the family) and the Quranic verse 33:56 debated between Hanafis and Shafi'is.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Nasa'i: 'Say: O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each proof supports the ruling. The hadith shows the recommended form; the verse is interpreted by Hanafis as 'submit to his decree,' not as a command for verbal salam.
The wajh al-dalalah for the hadith is that it provides the manner, not the obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing school (al-Shafi'i) and their proof: the apparent command in 33:56 makes salam wajib.
The dispute is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Show why the Hanafi position is mufta bihi: reliance on the interpretation of the verse and the weight of their school's methodology, as cited from al-Nihayah and Mabsut.
The commentator favors the Hanafi view, and the fatwa follows that.

Source Text

قوله : (وعلى آله وأصحابه) كذا في النسخ والظاهر أن المصنف سقط من قلمه فتوهم ذكره فعطف عليه، أو من الناسخ الأول والصلاة هنا هي المأمور بها في خبر أمرنا أن نصلي عليك، فكيف نصلي ؟ فقال : قولوا اللهم صل على محمد الخ لا مطلق الصلاة، والفرق بينهما أن مطلق الصلاة معناه الرحمة والصلاة المأمور بها معناها طلب الرحمة لأنها من مخلوق، فيلاحظ كونها مأموراً بها ليحصل بها امتثال الأمر فتكون أتم من غيرها وقيل: معناها العطف، وهي فرض في العمر مرة واحدة وتقوم مقامها الصلاة الواقعة في مكتوبة، أو غيرها بعد البلوغ وتجب كلما ذكر على أحد قولين وتسن في كل تشهد أخير من الفرض، وفي كل تشهد نقل إلا في سنة الظهر القبلية، والجمعة القبلية والبعدية، وتندب في أوقات الإمكان وتحرم على الحرام، وتكره عند فتح التاجر متاعه، ولا يكره أفرادها عن السلام على الأصح عندنا، وهذا الخلاف في حق نبينا أما في حق غيره من الأنبياء، فلا خلاف في عدم كراهة الأفراد لأحد من العلماء ذكره الحموي محشى الإشباه، وظاهر ما في النهاية من كتاب الصلاة أنه لا يجب السلام لأنه جعل الوجوب قول الشافعي : وأما قوله تعالى: (وسلموا فالمراد منه سلموا لقضائه كذا في مبسوط شيخ الإسلام والظاهر أن ذكر الآل والأصحاب مندوب أما الأصحاب، فظاهر لأنهم سلفنا، وقد أمرنا بالترضي عنهم ونهينا عن لعنهم، وأما الآل فلقوله : (لا تصلوا علي الصلاة البتراء قالوا: وما الصلاة البتراء يا رسول الله قال : تقولون اللهم صل على محمد، وتمسكون، بل قولوا: اللهم صل على محمد وعلى آل محمد ذكره الفاسي وغيره، والمراد بالآل هنا سائر أمة الإجابة مطلقاً، وقوله : (آل محمد كل تقي) حمل على التقوى من الشرك لأن المقام الدعاء، ونقل اللفاني في شرح جوهرته أنه يطلق على مؤمني بني هاشم أشراف والواحد شريف كما هو مصطلح السلف، وإنما حدث تخصيص الشريف بولد الحسن والحسين في مصر خاصة في عهد الفاطميين قال : ويجب إكرام الأشراف، ولو تحقق فرع الشجرة منها ولو مال وقوله وأصحابه جمع صاحب بمعنى صحابي لأن به سيبويه، ومثله بصاحب وأصحاب وارتضاه الزمخشري والرضي، وأبو حيان، وهو عند جمهور الأصوليين من طالت صحبته متبعاً مدة يثبت معها إطلاق صاحب فلان عرفاً بلا تحديد في الأصح ولذا صح نفيه عن الوافد اتفاقاً إذ يقال ليس صحابياً، بل وفد وارتحل من ساعته ، وقيل لا يشترط قال في التحرير: وينبني عليه ثبوت عدالة غير الملازم فلا يحتاج إلى التزكية، أو يحتاج وعلى هذا المذهب جرى الحنفية لأن فسقهم فاعلاً يجمع على أفعال صرح
His statement: (and upon his family and companions) — thus in the copies. Apparently the author dropped from his pen and imagined mentioning it and then joined it, or from the first scribe. And 'prayer' here is the one commanded in the report: 'We were commanded to pray upon you, so how should we pray?' He said: 'Say: O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad...' not absolute prayer. The difference between them is that absolute prayer means mercy, while the commanded prayer means seeking mercy because it is from a created being, so it is observed to be commanded to fulfill the order, thus it is more complete than others. It is said its meaning is affection. It is fard once in a lifetime, and it is fulfilled by the prayer occurring in an obligatory prayer or other after puberty. It becomes obligatory every time he is mentioned according to one of two opinions. It is sunnah in every final tashahhud of fard, and in every tashahhud of nafl except the sunnah before zuhr and before and after Jumu'ah. It is recommended at times of possibility, forbidden during haram, disliked when a merchant opens his goods. It is not disliked to send it alone without salam according to the more correct view in our school. This difference of opinion is regarding our Prophet; as for other prophets, there is no difference in not disliking its isolation from any scholar, as mentioned by al-Hamawi in hashiat al-Ashbah. The apparent meaning in al-Nihayah from the book of prayer is that salam is not obligatory because he made obligation the saying of al-Shafi'i. As for the verse 'and offer salutations' [Quran 33:56], the meaning intended is 'submit to His decree' as in Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam. And it is apparent that mentioning the family and companions is recommended. As for companions, it is clear because they are our predecessors, and we are commanded to be pleased with them and forbidden from cursing them. As for the family, due to his saying: 'Do not send a truncated prayer upon me.' They said: 'What is the truncated prayer, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'You say: O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad, and stop. Rather say: O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad.' Mentioned by al-Fasi and others. The meaning of 'al' here is absolutely all of the responding ummah. His statement: 'The family of Muhammad is every pious one' is interpreted as piety from shirk because the context is supplication. Al-Laffani transmitted in Sharh al-Jawharah that it is applied to the believers of Banu Hashim, nobles, the singular being 'sharif' as in the terminology of the Salaf; the specification of 'sharif' to the descendants of Hasan and Husayn occurred only in Egypt during the Fatimid era. He said: It is obligatory to honor the nobles, even if a branch of the tree is verified from them, even if wealth. And his statement 'and his companions,' plural of 'sahib' meaning 'sahabi' because according to Sibawayh and similar to 'sahib' and 'ashab' as approved by Zamakhshari, Radi, and Abu Hayyan. According to the majority of usul scholars, it is a person whose companionship was long, following for a period that establishes the usage of 'so-and-so's companion' customarily without definition, the most correct view. Hence it is valid to deny it of a visitor by consensus, as it is said 'he is not a Sahabi, rather he visited and departed immediately.' Some said it is not conditional. Al-Tahrir says: Upon this depends the establishment of the probity of one who is not a constant companion—whether he needs tazkiyah or not. And on this madhhab the Hanafis have proceeded because their sin...
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the ruling on sending blessings (salāt) and salutations (salām) upon the Prophet, his family, and companions. The commentator (al-Tahtawi) begins by noting an apparent textual issue with the author's wording. He then clarifies that 'salāt' here refers to the specific commanded form, which is different from absolute mercy. The ruling is that salāt upon the Prophet is fard once in a lifetime, sunnah in tashahhud, and recommended at other times. Salām is not obligatory according to the Hanafi school, contrary to al-Shafi'i. Mentioning the family and companions is recommended (mandūb). The commentator also defines 'āl' as all believers who respond (ummah al-ijābah) or specifically the pious of Banu Hashim, and 'sahābī' as one who accompanied the Prophet for a considerable time, not a mere visitor. The Hanafi position is that salām is not wajib, and the definition of Sahabi has implications for probity and tazkiyah.

Key Terms
صلاة (salāt): In this context, the commanded prayer upon the Prophet, which is a supplication for mercy distinct from absolute mercy.
سلام (salām): Verbal salutation upon the Prophet.
آل (āl): Generally, the believing community (ummah al-ijābah) or specifically pious individuals from Banu Hashim.
صحابي (sahābī): A person who accompanied the Prophet for a prolonged period in following him, such that customarily he is called a companion; a brief visit does not qualify.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is sending salāt upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) obligatory?
A) Every time he is mentioned.
B) Once in a lifetime.
C) In every prayer.
D) It is never obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between salat (fard once in lifetime) and salam (not wajib), and emphasizes including the family and companions in blessings as recommended.

Water Mixed with Pure Solids: Thickness and Flow
Defines ghalabah for solids mixed with water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ghalabah for pure solids mixed with water and apply it to determine the validity of wudu.

Core Idea
Water mixed with pure solids remains valid for wudu unless it becomes thick and ceases to flow.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah refines the criterion for when water mixed with pure solids becomes invalid for wudu. The key is ghalabah (predominance), defined for solids as loss of thinness and fluidity. Even if color, taste, or smell change, as long as the water remains thin and flowing, wudu is valid. This distinction is a unique Hanafi position supported by the hadith of sidr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions for ghalabah in solids
The passage states that predominance occurs when the water loses its thinness (so it cannot be wrung from cloth) and loses its fluidity (so it does not flow over limbs like water). Both must be present for the water to become invalid.
This is the Hanafi criterion; other schools use a different standard.
2
Understand the exception for cleaning agents
If the solid is used for cleaning (like sidr or soap) and the water is cooked with it, the water may become thick yet remains valid. This is proven by the Prophet's command to use water and sidr for ghusl.
Cooking with cleaning agents does not invalidate even if water thickens.
3
Apply the criterion to the hadith evidence
The hadith in Bukhari and Muslim shows that water mixed with sidr (which changes its attributes) was used for ghusl. This establishes that attribute change alone does not invalidate; only ghalabah as defined does.
The hadith is ahad but accepted as proof for this ruling.
4
Distinguish from the Shafi'i position
Shafi'is generally consider any change in water's attributes sufficient to invalidate it. Hanafis restrict invalidation to loss of thinness and flow. The practical difference appears when water is colored or scented but remains thin and flowing.
This ikhtilaf is recognized as legitimate within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأنه إذا برد ثخن كما إذا طبخ بما يقصد به النظافة كالسدر وصار به ثخيناً وإن بقي على الرقة جاز به الوضوء ولما كان تقييد الماء يحصل بأحد الأمرين كمال الإمتزاج بتشرب النبات، أو الطبخ بما ذكرناه بين الثاني، وهو غلبة الممتزج بقوله (أو بغلبة غيره) أي غير الماء (عليه) أي على الماء ولما كانت الغلبة مختلفة بإختلاف المخالط بغير طبخ ذكر ملخص ما جعله المحققون ضابطاً في ذلك فقال : ( والغلبة) تحصل (في مخالطة) الماء لشيء من (الجامدات الطاهرات (بإخراج الماء عن رقته فلا ينعصر عن الثوب (و) إخراجه عن (سيلانه) فلا يسيل على الأعضاء سيلان الماء (و) أما إذا بقي على رقته وسيلانه فإنه (لا يضر) أي لا يمنع جواز الوضوء به تغير أوصافه كلها بجامد خالطه بدون طبخ كزعفران وفاكهة وورق شجر ) لما في البخاري ومسلم أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أمر بغسل الذي وهو محرم بماء وسدر وأمر قيس بن عاصم حين أسلم أن يغتسل بماء وسدر
Because if it cools it thickens, as if it is cooked with something intended for cleanliness like sidr and becomes thick by it, and if it remains thin, wudu is permissible with it. And since restriction of water occurs by one of two matters: complete blending through absorption of plant, or cooking as we mentioned, he explained the second, which is predominance of the mixture by his saying: 'or by predominance of another' i.e. other than water 'over it' i.e. over water. And since predominance varies according to the mixture without cooking, he mentioned a summary of what the verifying scholars made a criterion in that, so he said: 'And predominance occurs in mixing water with something from pure solids by the water losing its thinness so it cannot be wrung from cloth, and losing its fluidity so it does not flow over the limbs like water flows. But if it remains in its thinness and fluidity, then it does no harm, i.e. does not prevent the permissibility of wudu with it, even if all its attributes change by a solid mixed without cooking, like saffron, fruit, and tree leaves.' Due to what is in Bukhari and Muslim that the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم ordered washing the one in ihram with water and sidr, and ordered Qays ibn 'Asim when he embraced Islam to perform ghusl with water and sidr.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) from al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah, defining when mixing water with pure solids renders it invalid for wudu. The key concept is 'ghalabah' (predominance), which for solids means two things: the water becomes thick (not wringable from cloth) and loses its fluidity (does not flow over limbs). However, if the water remains thin and flowing, wudu is valid even if all three attributes (color, taste, smell) change—e.g., saffron or fruit. Exception: if the solid is used for cleaning (like sidr or soap), cooking is allowed and the water may become thick yet remains valid because the intent is purification, as proven by hadith. The commentator refines the matn by clarifying the two causes of restriction (tamyeez): complete blending through absorption or cooking, and predominance of the mixture. The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
الغلبة (al-ghalabah): Predominance of the mixed substance over water such that water loses its thinness and fluidity.
الجامدات الطاهرات (al-jamadat al-tahirat): Pure solid substances that are not najis (impure), e.g., saffron, fruit, sidr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does water mixed with a pure solid (like saffron) become invalid for wudu?
A) Whenever any attribute (color, taste, smell) changes.
B) Only if it becomes thick and loses its fluidity.
C) Only if the solid is cooked with the water.
D) Only if the water becomes colored.

Key Takeaway
Water mixed with pure solids remains valid for wudu as long as it stays thin and flows, even if its color, taste, or smell change.

The Rule of Ghalabah When Water is Mixed with Pure Liquids
Defines ghalabah for liquids with attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of ghalabah to determine the validity of wudu when water is mixed with a pure liquid, based on the number of attributes of that liquid.

Core Idea
Predominance (ghalabah) is measured by the appearance of one or two attributes, depending on how many attributes the liquid has.

This lesson focuses on the Hanafi criterion for when water mixed with a pure liquid becomes invalid for wudu. The rule is precise and depends on the number of attributes (color, taste, smell) of the liquid that mixes with water. Understanding this rule is essential for correctly judging the permissibility of wudu in everyday situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the liquid and its attributes
Determine what type of pure liquid is mixed with the water. Identify its attributes: color, taste, and smell.
Some liquids have one, two, or three attributes.
2
Count the liquid's total attributes
Count how many of the three attributes (color, taste, smell) the liquid possesses. For example, milk has color and taste but no smell, so it has two attributes.
The Hanafi school uses this count to apply the ghalabah rule.
3
Apply the ghalabah rule
If the liquid has one attribute, the appearance of that attribute constitutes ghalabah. If it has two attributes, the appearance of any one of them constitutes ghalabah. If it has three attributes, the appearance of any two constitutes ghalabah.
Vinegar has three attributes; two must appear to invalidate wudu.
4
Determine the validity of wudu
If ghalabah occurs (i.e., the required number of attributes appear in the water), wudu is invalid. If not, wudu is valid.
The ruling assumes the liquid itself is pure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والغلبة تحصل في مخالطة المائعات بظهور وصف واحد كلون فقط أو طعم من مائع له وصفان فقط أي لا ثالث له ومثل ذلك بقوله كاللبن له اللون والطعم فإن لم يوجد أجاز به الوضوء وإن وجد أحدهما لم يجز كما لو كان المخالط له وصف واحد فظهر وصفه كبعض البطيخ ليس له إلا وصف واحد و قوله لا رائحة له زيادة إيضاح لعلمه من بيان الوصفين و الغلبة توجد بظهور وصفين من مائع له أوصاف ثلاثه وذلك كالخل له لون وطعم وريح فأي وصفين منها ظهرا منعا صحة الوضوء، والواحد منها لا يضر لقلته والغلبة في مخالطة المائع الذي لا وصف له يخالف الماء بلون أو طعم أو ريح كالماء المستعمل فإنه بالإستعمال لم يتغير له طعم
And predominance occurs in mixing with liquids by the appearance of one attribute (color only or taste) from a liquid that has only two attributes, i.e. no third. And he exemplified that with his saying: like milk, it has color and taste; if neither exists, wudu is permissible with it, but if one of them exists, it is not permissible. Similarly, if the mixture has only one attribute, and its attribute appears, like some melons which have only one attribute. And his saying: 'it has no smell' is an additional clarification, known from the explanation of two attributes. And predominance occurs by the appearance of two attributes from a liquid that has three attributes, such as vinegar: it has color, taste, and smell. So whichever two of them appear, they prevent the validity of wudu, and one of them does not harm due to its smallness. And predominance in mixing with a liquid that has no attribute differing from water in color, taste, or smell, like used water, for it has not changed in taste by use.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from al-Tahtawi explaining the Hanafi criterion for when water mixed with pure liquids becomes invalid. The rule depends on the number of attributes the liquid has: if it has two attributes (like milk: color and taste), the appearance of just one attribute (e.g., color) constitutes ghalabah and invalidates wudu. If the liquid has three attributes (like vinegar: color, taste, smell), then appearance of any two invalidates. If it has one attribute (like some melons or rose water: only taste or only smell), then appearance of that one attribute invalidates. The passage also addresses used water (al-ma' al-musta'mal): it is considered a liquid with no attributes of its own (since it was originally pure water and did not change attributes by use in wudu/ghusl). Therefore, mixing used water with pure water does not cause ghalabah unless the used water itself becomes predominant in quantity. The commentary on page 26 further discusses the practical ruling regarding small water reservoirs (fasaqi) in schools: as long as the used water is not predominant, wudu and ghusl are valid. This is based on the preferred fatwa position that used water is not najis.

Key Terms
المائعات (al-mawa'i'): Liquids other than water that are pure and mix with water.
الغلبة (al-ghalabah): Predominance of a pure liquid in water, determined by the appearance of its attributes according to a specific rule.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if water is mixed with a liquid that has three attributes, and only two of those attributes appear?
A) Wudu is valid because one attribute is missing.
B) Wudu is invalid because two attributes constitute ghalabah for a three-attribute liquid.
C) Wudu is invalid because any change invalidates.
D) Wudu is valid only if the liquid is in the majority.

Key Takeaway
For water mixed with a pure liquid, wudu is invalid only when the required number of the liquid's attributes appear, as per the Hanafi ghalabah rule.

Used Water (al-Ma' al-Musta'mal) and Its Effect on Wudu
Ruling on used water and its mixing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the Hanafi ruling on the validity of wudu with used water and apply the rule of quantity predominance for used water.

Core Idea
Used water is pure and purifying unless it becomes predominant in quantity, not by attribute appearance.

This lesson focuses on used water (al-ma' al-musta'mal), water that has been used for wudu or ghusl. The Hanafi school holds a specific position: used water is pure and can be used for wudu as long as it does not become the majority in a mixture. This contrasts with other schools and clarifies a common source of doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify used water
Water that has been used for wudu or ghusl (i.e., has touched a limb in worship) but has not changed in its attributes (color, taste, smell).
Used water is still water; it has no additional attributes.
2
Understand the Hanafi position
Used water is pure (tahir) and purifying (mutahhir) according to the preferred view. It does not become musta'mal in the Shafi'i sense.
Some older narrations considered it najis, but the mufta bihi is that it is pure.
3
Apply the rule for used water mixing
When used water mixes with fresh water, since used water has no attributes different from water, ghalabah is not determined by attributes. Instead, quantity matters: if used water becomes the majority, the mixture is considered used water and wudu with it is invalid.
If used water is the minority, the mixture retains the ruling of fresh water.
4
Determine validity of wudu
If used water is predominant in quantity, wudu is invalid. If not, wudu is valid.
This is based on the principle that used water is not purifying when it becomes the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And predominance occurs in mixing with liquids by the appearance of one attribute (color only or taste) from a liquid that has only two attributes, i.e. no third. And he exemplified that with his saying: like milk, it has color and taste; if neither exists, wudu is permissible with it, but if one of them exists, it is not permissible. If the liquid has three attributes (like vinegar: color, taste, smell), then appearance of any two invalidates. The passage also addresses used water (al-ma' al-musta'mal): it is considered a liquid with no attributes of its own (since it was originally pure water and did not change attributes by use in wudu/ghusl). This is based on the preferred fatwa position that used water is not najis.

Key Terms
الماء المستعمل (al-ma' al-musta'mal): Water that has been used for wudu or ghusl (i.e., that has touched a limb in worship) but remains unchanged in attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Ruling on the Su'r of Cats: Dislike Despite Hadith Permission
Ruling on cat su'r with hadith and analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of domestic and wild cats and explain the evidence and the rationale for the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Cat su'r is pure but disliked because cats do not avoid impurity; wild cat su'r is impure.

A well-known hadith narrated by At-Tirmidhi mentions that cats are among the animals that go around houses, implying their leftover water is permissible. However, the Hanafi school qualifies this with a ruling of discreet dislike (makruh tanzihan) due to cats' habits. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the reasoning behind the dislike, and the distinction between domestic and wild cats, along with related practical implications for prayer and eating leftover food.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
State clearly what the passage is ruling on: the su'r (leftover water or food) of a cat. Determine the degree of purity or impurity according to the Hanafi school.
The ruling differs for domestic cats (tawwafat) and wild cats (al-hirrah al-bariyyah).
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the proof cited in the passage: the hadith reported by At-Tirmidhi, which is considered hasan sahih. Note that this is a hadith ahad, so its evidence is zanni (probable).
The hadith is about cats being among the 'tawwafat' (those that go around), implying a general permission.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the Hanafi school extracts the ruling of dislike from a hadith that appears to permit. The school interprets the Prophet's action of lowering a vessel for a cat as specific to his time when cats' mouths were not assumed impure. The dislike arises from qiyas (analogy) to a child's hand: cats do not avoid impurities.
The analogy (qiyas) is with water into which a child dips his hand—pure but disliked if the child's hand is potentially impure.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Identify the Shafi'i position: they consider cat su'r absolutely pure (tahir) without any dislike, relying on the hadith as general permission without qualification.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a Shafi'i can use cat su'r for wudu without dislike, while a Hanafi should avoid it if alternative water is available (except for the poor under necessity).
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) for the school, as affirmed by Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah. The preference is based on combining the hadith with the principle of avoiding potential impurity (sadd al-dhara'i') and the general ruling on animals that do not avoid najasah.
The wild cat ruling is not disputed: without the 'illa (reason) of roaming, its su'r is najis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والطوافات، قال الترمذي حديث حسن صحيح، ولكن يكره سؤرها تنزيهاً على الأصح لأنها لا تتحامى عن النجاسة كماء غمس صغير يده فيه وحمل إصغاء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لها الإناء على زوال ذلك الوهم بعمله بحالها في زمان لا يتوهم نجاسة فمها بنجس تناولته والهرة البرية سؤرها نجس لفقد علة الطواف فيها ويكره أن تلحس الهرة كف إنسان، ثم يصلي قبل غسله، أو يأكل بقية ما أكلت منه ، إن كان غنياً يجد غيره ولا يكره أكله للفقير للضرورة
And cats (that roam around houses). At-Tirmidhi said: 'A hasan sahih hadith.' But its su'r is disliked (makruh tanzihan) according to the most correct view, because it does not avoid impurity, like water into which a child has dipped his hand. And the Prophet's (peace be upon him) act of lowering the vessel for the cat is interpreted as removing that misconception due to his action in his time when there was no assumption of its mouth being impure by something impure it ingested. The su'r of a wild cat is impure because it lacks the attribute of roaming. And it is disliked for a cat to lick a person's hand, then he prays before washing it, or eats the remainder of what it ate from, if he is wealthy and finds other food. It is not disliked for a poor person to eat it due to necessity.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on the leftover water (su'r) of cats. The author first mentions the hadith narrated by At-Tirmidhi (hasan sahih) about cats being among those that go around (tawwafat), implying their su'r is pure. However, the preferred view in the Hanafi school is that it is makruh tanzihan (slightly disliked) because cats do not avoid impurities, similar to water touched by a child's unwashed hand. The Prophet's act of lowering a vessel for a cat is explained as specific to his time when there was no worry about impurity. For wild cats (al-hirrah al-bariyyah), the su'r is impure (najis) because they lack the habit of roaming around houses. Additionally, if a cat licks a person's hand, it is disliked to pray without washing that hand, or for a wealthy person to eat the leftover food; but a poor person may eat it out of necessity.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): Leftover water or food after an animal or person has drunk or eaten from it.
الهرة البرية (al-hirrah al-bariyyah): Wild cat that does not roam around human dwellings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the su'r of a domestic cat according to the Hanafi school?
A) Pure (tahir) without any dislike
B) Pure but makruh tanzihan
C) Impure (najis)
D) Permissible only for poor people

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules cat su'r as pure but makruh tanzihan, except wild cats whose su'r is impure, based on the cat's nature and the hadith interpreted with caution.

6 min
Ruling on Su'r of Chicken and Birds of Prey
Explains the ruling on su'r of chickens and birds of prey with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of a roaming chicken and a bird of prey, and explain the istihsan-based exception to the qiyas that would deem it impure.

Core Idea
A bird's beak is dry bone, so its su'r is pure by istihsan, unlike a land predator's wet tongue.

The su'r (leftover water) of animals is categorized based on the animal's condition. Chickens and birds of prey pose a special case: their meat is prohibited, but their su'r is not automatically impure. In this passage, the Hanafi school explains why the su'r is merely disliked when there is doubt, and pure when certainty exists, using istihsan to override qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage discusses two types: a roaming chicken (mukhallah) and birds of prey (siba' al-tayr). Note the linguistic clarification for 'dajaja'.
Mukhallah is a chicken that roams freely in filth.
2
State the ruling for each category
For both, the su'r is disliked (makruh tanzih) when the cleanliness of the beak is unknown. If the beak is known to be pure (e.g., confined chicken or certainty about the bird's beak), there is no dislike.
Dislike is due to doubt, not inherent impurity.
3
Recognize the qiyas (analogy)
By analogy to predatory land animals (siba' al-baha'im), whose su'r is najis due to impure saliva and prohibition of meat, the su'r of birds of prey should also be najis.
Both have prohibited meat, but the 'illa (effective cause) differs.
4
Apply istihsan (juristic preference)
The Hanafi school overrides the qiyas using istihsan because birds drink with their beaks (dry bone), not with tongues wet with saliva. Therefore, the su'r is ruled pure.
Istihsan is based on a subtle difference in the 'illa.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school rules the su'r of these birds as pure (tahir) without any dislike, even when doubtful, whereas the Hanafi school adds dislike when uncertain.
This difference arises from varying levels of caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره سؤر (الدجاجة) بتثليث الدال وتاؤها للوحدة لا للتأنيث والدجاج مشترك بين الذكر والأنثى والدجاجة الأنثى خاصة، ولهذا لو حلف لا يأكل لحم دجاجة لا يحنث بلحم الديك ويكره سؤر (المخلاة) التي تجول في القاذورات ولم يعلم طهارة منقارها من نجاسته فكره سؤرها للشك فإن لم يكن كذلك فلا كراهة فيه بأن حبست فلا يصل منقارها لقذر (و) سؤر (سباع الطير كالصقر والشاهين والحدأة والرخم والغراب مكروه لأنها تخالط الميتات والنجاسات فأشبهت الدجاجة المخلاة حتى لو تيقن أنه لا نجاسة على منقارها لا يكره سؤرها، وكان القياس نجاسته لحرمة لحمها كسباع البهائم لكن طهارته استحسان لأنها تشرب بمنقارها، وهو عظم طاهر، وسباع البهائم تشرب بلسانها، وهو مبتل بلعابها النجس
And the su'r of a chicken (the word dajaja has three possible vowelizations; its ta is for the singular, not feminine; dajaj is common between male and female; dajaja is specifically female. Hence if someone swears not to eat the meat of 'dajaja', he does not break his oath by eating the meat of a rooster). And the su'r of a chicken that roams (al-mukhallah) which moves about in filth and the purity of its beak is not known from impurity is disliked due to doubt. If it is not so (i.e., it does not roam in filth), then there is no dislike, such as if it is confined so its beak does not reach filth. And the su'r of birds of prey like the falcon, peregrine, kite, vulture, and crow is disliked because they mix with dead animals and impurities, thus resembling a roving chicken. Even if one is certain there is no impurity on its beak, its su'r is not disliked. The analogy (qiyas) would be that its su'r is impure due to the prohibition of its meat like predatory land animals, but its purity is istihsan because they drink with their beaks, which are clean bone, whereas predatory land animals drink with their tongues, which are wet with impure saliva.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage covers two categories: First, the chicken (dajaja). The author clarifies linguistic points: the word can be pronounced three ways, and 'dajaja' is specifically the female. The su'r of a chicken that roams freely in filthy places (mukhallah) is disliked (makruh) because its beak may be impure. If the chicken is confined and its beak does not touch filth, then no dislike. Second, birds of prey (siba' al-tayr) such as falcons, vultures, crows: their su'r is disliked because they eat carrion and impurities, similar to a roving chicken. If one is certain the beak is pure, then no dislike. Analogically (qiyas), the su'r should be impure like predatory land animals, but the Hanafi school rules it pure by istihsan because birds drink with their beaks (bone, not wet with saliva), while land predators drink with their tongues (wet with impure saliva).

Key Terms
مخلاة (mukhallah): A chicken that roams freely in the streets and pecks at filth.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to a stronger evidence or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the su'r of a bird of prey considered pure (tahir) by istihsan despite the prohibition of its meat?
A) Because its meat is halal
B) Because it drinks with its beak which is clean bone
C) Because it avoids impurities
D) Because it is a bird, not a land animal

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to override qiyas when there is a clear difference in the 'illa (effective cause), such as beak vs. tongue, leading to purity of bird su'r despite prohibition of its meat.

Ruling on Su'r of Domestic Animals and Insects
States ruling on su'r based on flowing blood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on su'r of animals with and without flowing blood and apply the distinction to new cases.

Core Idea
Su'r of animals with flowing blood is disliked; without flowing blood, it is pure.

This passage clarifies the purity status of water left behind by small creatures that commonly inhabit human dwellings. The ruling hinges on whether the animal has 'flowing blood' (dam sa'il), which in Hanafi fiqh determines ritual impurity. Understanding this distinction helps avoid unnecessary scruples or neglect in daily purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
The passage addresses the su'r (leftover water) of specific animals. Determine that this is a matter of taharah (ritual purity), not muamalat.
2
Classify the animals by flowing blood
Group the animals into two categories: those with flowing blood (mice, snakes, geckos) and those without (scorpions, beetles, crickets).
Flowing blood means blood that flows when the animal is cut.
3
Apply the ruling to each category
For animals with flowing blood: su'r is makruh tanzih (disliked). For those without: su'r is pure and not disliked.
The dislike arises from the animal's impurity, not from the water itself.
4
Understand the rationale
Animals with flowing blood are considered impure (najis) when dead; their constant roaming makes their su'r disliked. Insects without flowing blood are not impure, so their su'r remains pure.
The ruling is based on the animal's inherent impurity, not on harm or disgust.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) سؤر (سواكن البيوت مما له دم سائل (كالفأرة)، والحية والوزعة مكروه للزوم طوافها، وحرمة لحمها النجس ، و (لا) كذلك سؤر (العقرب)، والخنفس، والصرصر لعدم نجاستها فلا كراهة فيه
And the su'r of domestic animals that have flowing blood like the mouse, snake, and gecko is disliked due to their necessity to roam and the prohibition of their impure meat. But not so the su'r of the scorpion, beetle, and cricket because they are not impure, so there is no dislike in it.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage addresses animals that live in human dwellings. Those with flowing blood (i.e., their blood flows when cut) such as mice, snakes, and geckos: their su'r is disliked (makruh) because they constantly roam around (like cats) and their meat is prohibited and considered impure. As for insects like scorpions, beetles, and crickets, they do not have flowing blood, so they are not considered impure (najis), and thus their su'r is not disliked; it is pure. The difference is based on the impurity of the animal itself. Note: The Hanafi school considers the mouse and similar animals to have flowing blood, hence their bodies are impure; scorpions, etc., do not have flowing blood, so they are considered pure.

Key Terms
دم سائل (dam sa'il): Blood that flows when the animal is cut; used to distinguish animals that are inherently impure (najis).
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water from a utensil after an animal has drunk from it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the su'r of a scorpion not disliked according to the passage?
A) Because it is a predator
B) Because it does not have flowing blood and is not impure
C) Because it avoids water
D) Because it is beneficial

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on su'r hinges on whether the animal possesses flowing blood: if it does, the water is disliked but not impure; if it does not, the water is pure.

Mashkuk Su'r: Definition and Ruling
Defines the fourth category of su'r: mashkuk, with expansion on the donkey case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mashkuk su'r, state its ruling (doubtful tahuriyya), and explain the reasoning based on necessity and common occurrence.

Core Idea
Donkey saliva is pure but its su'r creates doubt in water's purifying ability, requiring tayammum for certainty.

After covering pure, impure, and disliked su'r, we now encounter the fourth category: mashkuk (doubtful). This category arises when an animal's saliva is pure but its interaction with water creates uncertainty about the water's ability to purify. The classic example is the donkey, whose pure sweat and saliva, when mixed with a small amount of water, render the water mashkuk in tahuriyya.

Guided Path
1
Define mashkuk su'r
Understand that mashkuk su'r is water that is pure (tahir) but its ability to purify (tahuriyya) is doubtful.
The doubt is not about purity but about purifying power.
2
Identify the cause of doubt
The doubt stems from balancing necessity (darura) and common occurrence (balwa). The donkey cannot be fully avoided (like a cat), but its necessity is less than a cat's. Thus, two opposing evidences are reconciled by keeping the water pure but doubting its purifying ability.
This is the talil (reasoning) behind the ruling.
3
State the ruling on donkey saliva/sweat
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that donkey sweat and saliva are pure in themselves. They do not make the body or clothes impure.
This is uncontested within the school.
4
Determine the ruling when mixed with water
If donkey saliva or sweat falls into a small amount of water (less than two qullahs), the water becomes mashkuk: it is pure but its purifying ability is doubted.
The doubt only affects tahuriyya, not tahara.
5
Apply the precautionary measure
Because the water's purifying ability is doubtful, a person should use that water for wudu but also perform tayammum to ensure purification with certainty.
This is the exercise of caution (ihtiyat).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) القسم (الرابع) سؤر (مشكوك) أي متوقف (في) حكم (طهوريته) . . . قوله: (أي) متوقف في حكم طهوريته قال شيخ الإسلام خواهر زاده: الأصح أن دليل الأشكال هو التردد في الضرورة، والبلوى المسقطتين للنجاسة فإن الحمار يربط في الدور ويشرب من الأواني المستعملة، ويخالط الناس في ركوبه فأشبه الهرة في عدم إمكان مجانبته فسقطت نجاسة لعابه للحرج لكن ليست فيه كالضرورة في الهرة لأنها أشد مخالطة منه لدخولها في المضايق دون الحمار ، فلو لم يكن فيه ضرورة أصلاً، كان كالكلب في الحكم بالنجاسة بلا إشكال، ولو كانت الضرورة فيه كضرورة الهرة كان مثلها في سقوط النجاسة لذلك، وحيث ثبتت الضرورة من وجه دون وجه قيل بالشك في طهورية سؤره للاحتياط، وعدم الحرج في ذلك عملاً بالدليلين بقدر الإمكان وإعمال الدليلين أولى من إهمالهما عند عدم المرجح قال في البحر والمعتمد أن كلا من عرق الحمار، ولعابه ظاهر وإذا أصاب الثوب، أو البدن لا ينجسه، وإذا وقع في الماء القليل صار مشكوكاً وان الشك في جانب اللعاب والعرق أي في ذاتهما متعلق بالطهارة وفي جانب السؤر متعلق بالطهورية فقط، ولا شك في الطهارة لأن الماء ظاهر بيقين وقد خالطه مشكوك في طهارته، وهو اللعاب، أو العرق فلا ينجس، بالشك، ولكن أورث شكاً في طهوريته للاحتياط، حتى لو اختلط هذا السؤر بماء قليل جاز الوضوء به من غير شك ما لم يساوه، كما في مخالطة الماء المستعمل اهـ . قوله: (قلم يحكم الخ) أي فاحتجنا معه إلى التيمم لتحقق الرفع بمطهر يقيناً
And the fourth category: doubtul su'r, i.e., suspended in the ruling of its purifying ability. ... He said: (i.e., suspended in the ruling of its purifying ability). Shaykh al-Islam Khwāharzādah said: The most correct is that the cause of the doubt is the hesitation between necessity and common occurrence that remove impurity. Indeed, the donkey is tied in houses and drinks from used vessels, and mixes with people when ridden, so it resembles the cat in the impossibility of avoiding it, so the impurity of its saliva is dropped due to hardship. But it does not have the same level of necessity as the cat because the cat mixes more intensely, entering narrow places unlike the donkey. So if there were no necessity at all, it would be like the dog in ruling of impurity without any doubt. And if the necessity were like that of the cat, it would be like it in dropping impurity. But since necessity is established in one way and not another, doubt in the purifying ability of its su'r is held for precaution, and there is no hardship in that, acting on both evidences as much as possible. Acting on both evidences is better than neglecting them when there is no preponderance. Al-Bahr says: The relied-upon position is that both the sweat and saliva of the donkey are pure in themselves. If they hit the garment or body, they do not make it impure. But if they fall into a small quantity of water, it becomes doubtful. And the doubt regarding the saliva and sweat i.e., in themselves, relates to purity, while regarding the su'r it relates only to purifying ability. There is no doubt about purity because water is certainly pure, and it has been mixed with something whose purity is doubtful, i.e., saliva or sweat, so it does not become impure by doubt. But it creates doubt in its purifying ability out of precaution. So if this su'r is mixed with a small amount of water, it is permissible to perform wudu with it without doubt as long as it does not equal it, similar to mixing with used water. And he said: (did not rule) i.e., we need tayammum together with it to ensure removal with a certainly purifying medium.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth category of su'r: mashkuk (doubtful), meaning that its ability to purify (tahuriyya) is uncertain. The author cites Khwāharzādah: The doubt arises from balancing two factors: necessity (darura) and common occurrence (balwa) that justify dropping impurity. The donkey (himar) is often kept in homes, drinks from vessels, and is ridden, so it resembles the cat in that it cannot be fully avoided; therefore, its saliva is not considered impure due to hardship. However, the necessity for the donkey is less than for the cat because the cat enters narrow spaces more. If there were no necessity, the saliva would be impure like a dog's. Since necessity is partial, the su'r is doubtful. The relied-upon view (from al-Bahr) is that donkey sweat and saliva are pure in themselves; they do not make clothes or body impure. But if they fall into a small amount of water (less than two qullahs), the water becomes mashkuk: it remains pure (tahir) but its ability to purify (tahuriyya) is doubted. Therefore, one should use such water for ablution together with tayammum to be certain of purification. The doubt does not cause impurity, only a precautionary ruling on tahuriyya.

Key Terms
مشكوك (mashkuk): Doubtful; a category of su'r whose tahuriyya (ability to purify) is uncertain, though the substance itself is pure.
طهورية (tahuriyya): The property of being purifying, i.e., able to remove ritual impurity (hadath) and filth (najasa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on water mixed with donkey saliva according to the relied-upon Hanafi view?
A) It becomes impure (najis)
B) It remains pure and purifying
C) It is pure but doubtful in its purifying ability
D) It becomes makruh tanzihan

Key Takeaway
Donkey su'r creates doubt in water's purifying ability, requiring tayammum for certainty, though the water itself remains pure.

Three Types of Doubt and Their Rulings
Categorizes doubt into three types with rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of doubt in Hanafi fiqh and apply the ruling of istishab (presumption of continuity) and majority (ghalaba) to each.

Core Idea
The ruling on doubt depends on the original state and the presence of a preponderant majority.

Doubt (shakk) in legal matters can lead to confusion, but the Hanafi school provides a clear framework. This lesson breaks down three categories of doubt, each with its own ruling based on whether the original status is prohibition or permission, and whether a majority tips the scale. Understanding these categories helps apply istishab and the principle of acting on the predominant condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of doubt
Read the passage and list the three categories: doubt on an originally prohibited thing, doubt on an originally permissible thing, and doubt whose origin is unknown.
2
Analyze the first type: doubt on prohibited origin
For example, a slaughtered sheep in a mixed population. The original presumption is prohibition unless Muslim slaughter is confirmed. If Muslims are the majority, the majority is followed and it becomes permissible.
3
Analyze the second type: doubt on permissible origin
For example, water that has changed color. The original state is purity, so it remains permissible for wudu regardless of the cause of change, until impurity is certain.
4
Analyze the third type: unknown origin
When most of one's property is unlawful but a specific item's origin is unknown. The sale is not unlawful (because the specific item's unlawfulness is not confirmed), but it is disliked to avoid falling into the unlawful.
5
Apply the principles of istishab and ghalaba
Istishab preserves the original status (prohibition or permission). Ghalaba (majority) overrides the original doubt when the majority supports one side.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه : مثل تعارض الخبرين الشك وقالوا إن الشك على ثلاثة أضرب شك طرأ على أصل حرام، وشك طرأ على أصل مباح وشك لا يعرف أصله، فالأول مثل أن يجد شاة مذبوحة في بلد فيها مسلمون ومجوس فلا تحل حتى يعلم أنها ذكاة مسلم لأن الأصل فيها الحرمة إذ حل الأكل يتوقف على تحقق الذكاة الشرعية، فصار حل الأكل مشكوكاً فلو كان الغالب فيها المسلمين جاز الأكل عملاً بالغالب المفيد للحل والثاني أن يجد ماء متغيراً، واحتمل أن يكون تغيره بنجاسة، أو طول مكث يجوز التطهير به عملاً بأصل الطهارة، والثالث أكثر ما له حرام لا تحرم مبايعته حيث لم يتحقق حرمة ما أخذه منه، ولكن يكره خوفاً من الوقوع في الحرام كذا في فتح القدير ، قاله أبو السعود في حاشية الإشباه.
Note: Doubt is like conflicting reports. They said: Doubt is of three types: doubt that occurs upon an originally prohibited thing, doubt that occurs upon an originally permissible thing, and doubt whose origin is unknown. The first is like finding a slaughtered sheep in a town containing Muslims and Magians; it is not lawful until one knows it is a Muslim's slaughter, because the original state is prohibition, since the lawfulness of eating depends on the legal slaughter being confirmed. So the lawfulness of eating becomes doubtful. If the majority are Muslims, it is permissible to eat, acting on the majority which yields permissibility. The second is like finding water that has changed, and it is possible that its change is due to impurity or due to lengthy storage; it is permissible to use it for purification, acting on the original state of purity. The third is that most of one's property is unlawful; the sale of it is not unlawful because the unlawfulness of what he took from it is not confirmed, but it is disliked out of fear of falling into the unlawful. So in Fath al-Qadir, and Abu al-Su'ud said it in Hashiyat al-Ashbah.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This note from the Hashiya addresses the legal effect of doubt by analogy to conflicting reports. The author presents three categories of doubt. The first is when doubt arises about something that was originally prohibited, like a slaughtered animal found in a mixed population. The original ruling is that it is not lawful unless slaughter by a Muslim is confirmed. However, if the majority of the population are Muslims, one may act on the presumption that it was lawfully slaughtered. The second type is doubt about something originally permissible, such as water whose color has changed. The original ruling of purity remains, so it may be used for purification unless impurity is confirmed. The third type is when most of a person's property is unlawful, but the specific item being sold is not known to be from the unlawful part. In this case, the sale is not prohibited, but it is disliked. This classification helps in applying the principle of istishab (presumption of continuity) and the consideration of majority (ghalaba).

Key Terms
شك (shakk): Doubt about the legal status of an item or act; unlike certainty, it does not change the original ruling unless a preponderance exists.
أصل حرام (asl haram): The default legal presumption that a thing is prohibited unless proven otherwise.
غالب (ghalib): The prevailing or majority situation; when doubt arises, the predominant condition may be used to determine the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on water that is found changed, but it is unknown whether the change is due to impurity or long storage?
A) It is considered impure because change indicates impurity.
B) It remains permissible for use because the original state of purity is presumed.
C) It requires further investigation before use.
D) It is disliked to use it.

Key Takeaway
The three categories of doubt show that the original status (istishab) governs unless a clear majority (ghalaba) overrides it.

Greeting by Bowing and Hand Gestures
Rulings on greeting by bowing and hand gestures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on greeting by bowing or lowering the head and identify why it is disliked.

Core Idea
Greeting by bowing mimics worship and is disliked; the sunna combines speech and gesture.

In this lesson, we examine two physical gestures used in greeting: bowing the head and gesturing with the hand alone. The Hanafi school rules both as disliked (makruh tanzihi) because they resemble acts of worship reserved for Allah or the practices of non-Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts
What are the two greeting gestures mentioned? Bowing (tahiyyah bi al-rukoo') and hand gesture (salam bi al-yad).
2
State the ruling
The author declares both as makruh tanzihi for everyone absolutely.
3
Understand the reason
Why are they disliked? Because bowing resembles the posture of prayer (rukoo'), and exclusive hand gesture imitates non-Muslims.
The sunna combines speech and gesture.
4
Note the exception
The disliked ruling applies when one confines to gesture alone; combining with speech is permissible.
Al-Shurunbulali mentions a hadith about combining speech and gesture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكان عمر يأخذ المصحف كل غداة، ويقبله وكان عثمان يقبله، ويمسحه على وجهه، وتقبيل الخبز قال أصحاب الشافعي رضي الله تعالى عنه : إنه بدعة مباحة، وقالوا: يكره بوسه وقواعدنا لا تأباه وفي رسالة المصافحة للشرنبلالي عن شيخ مشايخه الحانوتي : التحية بالركوع واسترخاء الرأس مكروهة لكل أحد مطلقاً، ومثله السلام باليد كما نصت عليه الحنفية اهـ قال الشرنبلالي : بعد ومحل كراهة الإشارة باليد إذا اقتصر عليها وذكر حديثاً يفيد أنه جمع بين اللفظ والإشارة، وفي شرح الوهبانية لابن الشحنة، وفي مشكل الآثار القيام لغيره ليس بمكروه لعينه إنما المكروه محبة القيام من الذي يقام له فإن لم يحب وقاموا له لا يكره لهم يعني جميعاً، قال : وقال القاضي البديع وقيام قارىء القرآن للقادم تعظيماً لا يكره إذا كان ممن يستحق التعظيم وقيل له أن يقوم بين يدي العالم تعظيماً له أما في غيره فلا يجوز، وقال ابن وهبان في شرحه والقيام يستحب في زماننا لما يورث تركه من والبغضاء والوعيد إنما هو في حق من يحب القيام بين يديه كما يفعله الترك، وفي أبي هريرة : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يجلس معنا في المسجد يحدثنا فإذا قام قمنا قياماً حتى نراه قد دخل بعض بيوت أزواجه، وعن واثلة دخل رجل إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو قاعد في المسجد فتزحزح له رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال الرجل : يا رسول الله إن في المكان سعة فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : إن للمسلم لحقاً رواهما البيهقي في الشعب وأما المعانقة وهي كما في القهستاني جعل كل منهما يده على عنق الآخر فقالا بكراهتها وأباحه أبو يوسف، وظاهر عبارة مواهب الرحمن اختياره حيث قال مقتصراً عليه ويبيح أي أبو يوسف للرجل معانقة مثله وتقبيله للمبرة بلا شهوة كالمصافحة، وتقبيل يد العالم والسلطان العادل للتبرك اهـ قالوا الخلاف فيما إذا لم يكن عليهما غير الإزار ، وأما إذا كان عليهما قميص أو جبة أو رداء مع الإزار، فلا بأس به بالإجماع، كما في رفع العوائق عن الشمني والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
And Umar would take the Quran every morning and kiss it, and Uthman would kiss it and wipe it on his face. And kissing bread: the followers of al-Shafi'i said it is an allowable innovation, and they said it is disliked to kiss it, and our principles do not forbid it. And in the treatise on handshake by al-Shurunbulali from his teacher al-Hanuti: greeting by bowing and lowering the head is disliked for everyone absolutely, and similarly greeting with the hand, as the Hanafis have stated. End. Al-Shurunbulali said: later, the place of disapproval of gesturing with the hand is when he confines to it, and he mentioned a hadith indicating that he combined speech and gesture. And in Sharh al-Whabbaniyya by Ibn al-Shihnah, and in Mushkil al-Athar: standing for another is not disliked in itself, rather the disliked thing is the love of standing from the one being stood for. If he does not like it and they stand for him, it is not disliked for them, meaning all. He said: And al-Qadi al-Badi' said: Standing of a reciter of Quran for a newcomer out of respect is not disliked if the newcomer is deserving of respect, and it was said that one may stand before a scholar to honor him; otherwise it is not permissible. And Ibn Wahban said in his commentary: Standing is recommended in our time because abandoning it causes enmity and hatred. The threat is only for one who loves people standing before him, as the Turks do. And from Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah would sit with us in the mosque and talk to us; when he stood, we would stand until we saw him enter one of his wives' houses. And from Wathila: A man entered upon the Messenger of Allah while he was sitting in the mosque, and the Messenger of Allah moved aside for him. The man said: O Messenger of Allah, there is plenty of room. The Prophet said: Indeed, the Muslim has a right. Both narrated by al-Bayhaqi in al-Shu'ab. As for embracing: it is, as in al-Qahistani, each putting his hand on the other's neck. The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad?) said it is disliked, and Abu Yusuf permitted it. The apparent wording of Mawahib al-Rahman indicates his choice: And Abu Yusuf permits a man to embrace his like and kiss him for piety without lust, like the handshake. And kissing the hand of a scholar and a just ruler for blessing. End. They said the disagreement is when they are wearing only an izār; but if they are wearing a shirt or a cloak or a wrap over the izār, then there is no harm by consensus, as in Raf' al-'Awa'iq by al-Shumunni. And Allah knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Great.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings about physical gestures of respect, presented as a commentary on the previous topic. It covers: (1) Kissing the Quran – The companions did it, so it is permissible by their practice. (2) Kissing bread – The Shafi'is consider it an innovation but permissible; the Hanafi position does not forbid it. (3) Greeting by bowing (ruckoo') or lowering the head – This is absolutely disliked for everyone, as it resembles acts of worship directed to other than Allah. Similarly, greeting solely by hand gesture (without speech) is disliked; the sunna is to combine speech and gesture. (4) Standing for another person – The ruling depends on intention. If the stood person loves it, it is disliked; if he does not love it and people stand spontaneously, it is not disliked. For a deserving person (scholar, parent), standing is recommended in our time to avoid discord. Hadith evidence shows the Prophet's companions stood as a sign of respect when he departed. (5) Moving aside to make room – The Prophet did it, indicating it is a good deed. (6) Embracing – Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said it is disliked when wearing only an izār (loincloth) due to skin contact; but if wearing a shirt or cloak, it is permissible by consensus. Abu Yusuf permitted it even without extra clothing when done for piety. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of weighing differences: the mufta bihi is often the more lenient view if it leads to brotherhood.

Key Terms
تحية بالركوع (tahiyyah bi al-rukoo'): Greeting by bowing the head or body, similar to the posture of rukoo' in prayer. Ruled makruh tanzihi.
السلام باليد (al-salam bi al-yad): Greeting solely by gesturing with the hand without saying the words of salam. Disliked when isolated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, greeting by bowing is:
A) Sunnah
B) Makruh tanzihi
C) Haram
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Bowing in greeting is disliked; the sunna greeting combines speech and gesture.

6 min
Standing for Others
Rulings on standing for another person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on standing for another person by distinguishing between the intention of the person being stood for and the act itself.

Core Idea
Standing for another is not inherently disliked; the key is the intention of the one being honored.

The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling on standing for someone: the act itself is not disliked, but if the person being stood for loves it, it becomes disliked. In our time, standing for scholars or those deserving respect is actually recommended to avoid enmity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
What is the act? Standing for another person. The default ruling: not disliked in itself (la yuqalu bi karahah li 'aynihi).
The disliked aspect is attached to the intention of the person being stood for.
2
Determine the intention of the honored
If the person being stood for loves to be stood for, then standing becomes disliked for those who stand. If he does not love it, then it is not disliked for them.
The ruling changes based on the intention (niyyah) of the one being honored.
3
Apply the exception for deserving persons
For scholars, parents, and those deserving respect, standing is recommended (mustahab) in our time because not standing may cause enmity and hatred.
Ibn Wahban says: 'Standing is recommended in our time because abandoning it causes enmity.'
4
Consider the evidence from hadith
The hadith of Abu Hurairah shows the Companions stood when the Prophet stood, out of respect. Also, the Prophet moved aside for a man, indicating the importance of honoring Muslims.
These actions are not obligatory but show respect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

محبة القيام (mahabbah al-qiyam): The love of being stood for. If present, it makes standing disliked.

Embracing: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Rulings on embracing (mu'anaqah) with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on embracing (mu'anaqah) and identify the conditions under which it is permissible or disliked.

Core Idea
Embracing is disliked when wearing only an izār, but permissible by consensus when clothed; Abu Yusuf permits it even without.

Embracing (mu'anaqah) is a physical expression of affection and respect. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it disliked when in minimal clothing, while Abu Yusuf permits it absolutely. The later fatwa prefers the permissive view, especially when clothed.

Guided Path
1
Define the act
What is embracing? Each person places their hands on the other's neck, as defined in al-Qahistani.
2
Identify the positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said it is disliked (makruh). Abu Yusuf permitted it.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Determine the scope of disagreement
The disagreement is when both are wearing only izār (loincloth). If they wear a shirt or cloak over the izār, there is consensus that it is permissible.
The ruling changes based on dress.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The later Hanafi scholars (al-Shurunbulali, Ibn Wahban) prefer Abu Yusuf's ruling, permitting embracing for piety without lust.
The mufta bihi is permission, especially when clothed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكان عمر يأخذ المصحف كل غداة، ويقبله وكان عثمان يقبله، ويمسحه على وجهه، وتقبيل الخبز قال أصحاب الشافعي رضي الله تعالى عنه : إنه بدعة مباحة، وقالوا: يكره بوسه وقواعدنا لا تأباه وفي رسالة المصافحة للشرنبلالي عن شيخ مشايخه الحانوتي : التحية بالركوع واسترخاء الرأس مكروهة لكل أحد مطلقاً، ومثله السلام باليد كما نصت عليه الحنفية اهـ قال الشرنبلالي : بعد ومحل كراهة الإشارة باليد إذا اقتصر عليها وذكر حديثاً يفيد أنه جمع بين اللفظ والإشارة، وفي شرح الوهبانية لابن الشحنة، وفي مشكل الآثار القيام لغيره ليس بمكروه لعينه إنما المكروه محبة القيام من الذي يقام له فإن لم يحب وقاموا له لا يكره لهم يعني جميعاً، قال : وقال القاضي البديع وقيام قارىء القرآن للقادم تعظيماً لا يكره إذا كان ممن يستحق التعظيم وقيل له أن يقوم بين يدي العالم تعظيماً له أما في غيره فلا يجوز، وقال ابن وهبان في شرحه والقيام يستحب في زماننا لما يورث تركه من والبغضاء والوعيد إنما هو في حق من يحب القيام بين يديه كما يفعله الترك، وفي أبي هريرة : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يجلس معنا في المسجد يحدثنا فإذا قام قمنا قياماً حتى نراه قد دخل بعض بيوت أزواجه، وعن واثلة دخل رجل إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو قاعد في المسجد فتزحزح له رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال الرجل : يا رسول الله إن في المكان سعة فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : إن للمسلم لحقاً رواهما البيهقي في الشعب وأما المعانقة وهي كما في القهستاني جعل كل منهما يده على عنق الآخر فقالا بكراهتها وأباحه أبو يوسف، وظاهر عبارة مواهب الرحمن اختياره حيث قال مقتصراً عليه ويبيح أي أبو يوسف للرجل معانقة مثله وتقبيله للمبرة بلا شهوة كالمصافحة، وتقبيل يد العالم والسلطان العادل للتبرك اهـ قالوا الخلاف فيما إذا لم يكن عليهما غير الإزار ، وأما إذا كان عليهما قميص أو جبة أو رداء مع الإزار، فلا بأس به بالإجماع، كما في رفع العوائق عن الشمني والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.

(5) Moving aside to make room – The Prophet did it, indicating it is a good deed. (6) Embracing – Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said it is disliked when wearing only an izār (loincloth) due to skin contact; but if wearing a shirt or cloak, it is permissible by consensus. Abu Yusuf permitted it even without extra clothing when done for piety. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of weighing differences: the mufta bihi is often the more lenient view if it leads to brotherhood.

Key Terms
معانقة (mu'anaqah): Embracing by placing each hand on the other's neck. Ruling: disliked if only izār on, permissible by consensus if clothed.
الإزار (al-izar): A waist-wrapper or loincloth. The minimal covering for men in the context of this ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is embracing permissible by consensus in the Hanafi school?
A) When both are wearing only an izār
B) When they wear a shirt or cloak over the izār
C) When it is done after prayer
D) When it is done with lust

Key Takeaway
Embracing is permissible in the Hanafi school, especially when clothed; the ikhtilaf is resolved in favor of permissibility.
