Burial Sunan: Scattering Soil and Shaping the Grave
Rulings on throwing earth and grave mound shape

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunan acts of burial and identify which actions are disliked (makruh) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The grave should be raised humped one handspan and watered – simplicity and preservation.

This lesson covers the recommended practices when burying a Muslim. The Prophet (peace be upon him) demonstrated how to scatter soil, the number of handfuls, and the shape of the grave mound. We will explore these sunan and the limits set by the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunan acts
From the text, list the actions: scattering soil, throwing three handfuls from the head side, making the grave musannam, and sprinkling water.
These are all mustahabb or sunnah.
2
Examine the proof (dalil)
The text cites the Prophet's action: he prayed over a funeral, then came to the grave and threw three handfuls from the head side. This is the basis for the sunna.
This is a fi'l (action) of the Prophet, which indicates recommendation in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the grave mound shape
The grave should be made musannam (humped like a camel's hump), not flat. This is the Hanafi view.
Some other schools prefer musattah (flat), but the Hanafi follow the humped shape.
4
Note the disliked actions
It is disliked (makruh) to add extra soil beyond what was dug out, and to raise the grave more than a handspan (shibr) above ground.
Excessive height resembles building and may be unlawful.
5
Recognize the permission to sprinkle water
Sprinkling water on the grave is not disliked but permitted to preserve the grave, especially in dry climates.
The Prophet himself did this for certain Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويهال التراب ستراً له، ويستحب أن يحثى ثلاثاً لما أنه صلى على جنازة، ثم أتى القبر فحثى عليه التراب من قبل رأسه ثلاثاً (ويسنم القبر) ويكره أن يزيد فيه على التراب الذي خرج منه ويجعله مرتفعاً عن الأرض قدر شبر، أو أكثر بقليل، ولا بأس برش الماء حفظاً له
And soil is scattered over it as a covering. It is recommended to throw three handfuls, because he (the Prophet, peace be upon him) prayed over a funeral, then came to the grave and threw soil upon it from the direction of his head three times. And the grave is made humped (musannam). It is disliked to increase in it beyond the soil that came out of it, and to make it rise above the ground about a handspan or slightly more. And there is no harm in sprinkling water to preserve it.
Source pages p. 610

Commentary
This passage covers multiple sunan and adab of burial. First, it is recommended to scatter soil into the grave as a cover. Then, those present should throw three handfuls of soil from the head side, following the Prophet's action. The grave mound should be raised in a humped shape (musannam), which is the Hanafi position (some say it is wajib, but the preferred view is mustahabb). The height should be about a handspan (shibr), and it is disliked to use soil other than what was dug from the grave, as that resembles building. Interestingly, sprinkling water on the grave is not disliked but rather encouraged, as the Prophet did for the graves of his son Ibrahim and Uthman ibn Maz'un. The water helps preserve the grave structure, especially in dry climates.

Key Terms
يسنم (yusannam): To make the grave mound in a humped shape, like the hump of a camel.
شبر (shibr): A handspan, approximately 20-25 cm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The grave should be simple: humped, about a handspan high, with water sprinkled, following the Prophet's example.

Prohibitions and Disliked Acts Regarding Grave Construction
Rulings on squaring graves, plastering, building, and writing on graves.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on squaring (tarbi'), plastering (tajsis), building, and writing on graves, and distinguish between haram, makruh, and permissible based on intent and timing.

Core Idea
Grave adornment is haram; preservation building is makruh; need permits writing on grave markers.

The Hanafi school prescribes specific etiquettes for grave construction, balancing reverence and the transient nature of the grave. This lesson examines the rulings on squaring graves, plastering, building structures, and inscribing markers, based on explicit prophetic prohibitions and later scholarly concessions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Acts and Their Default Rulings
List each act mentioned in the passage: squaring (tarbi'), plastering (tajsis), building for adornment (al-zina), building for preservation after burial, and writing on a preservation stone.
The passage states the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited tarbi', tajsis, and building on graves generally.
2
Determine the Hukm Level for Each Act
Tarbi' and tajsis are haram by explicit hadith. Building for adornment is also haram. Building for preservation after burial is makruh. Writing on a stone for identification is permissible.
The distinction hinges on the intent (adornment vs. preservation) and timing (before or after burial).
3
Examine the Prophetic Dalil
The hadith of Jabir (reported by Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) explicitly prohibits plastering, writing, and building on graves. This serves as the primary evidence for these prohibitions.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but the Hanafi school treats it as binding in this context.
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Preservation Building
Some Hanafis allow building for preservation completely, while others consider it makruh. The mufta bihi is makruh, though plastering with mud (tityan) is permissible per later fatawa.
The fatwa from al-Ghiyathiyyah permits mud plastering as a preservation measure.
5
Apply the Exception for Writing on Grave Markers
Despite the general prohibition, writing on a stone placed on the grave to preserve its trace is allowed due to necessity. This is an istihsan exception.
The passage explicitly states there is no harm in such writing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يربع) ولا يجصص لنهي النبي عن تربيع القبور وتجصيصها (ويحرم البناء عليه للزينة) لما روينا (ويكره) البناء عليه للأحكام بعد الدفن) لأنه للبقاء والقبر للفناء، وأما قبل الدفن فليس بقبر، وفي النوازل لا بأس بتطيينه، وفي الغيائية، وعليه الفتوى (ولا بأس أيضاً (بالكتابة) في حجر صين به القبر ووضع عليه لئلا يذهب الأثر
And it (the grave) is not to be made square (tarbi'), nor plastered (tajsis), due to the Prophet's prohibition of squaring graves and plastering them. And building upon it for adornment is haram, based on what we have narrated. And building upon it for preservation after burial is disliked, because it is for permanence while the grave is for annihilation. But before burial it is not a grave. And in al-Nawazil: there is no harm in plastering it with mud, and in al-Ghiyathiyyah the fatwa is upon this. And there is also no harm in writing on a stone by which the grave is preserved and placed upon it so that the trace is not lost.
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage covers additional prohibitions and disliked acts. First, it is prohibited (haram) to square the grave (tarbi') or to plaster it (tajsis), based on explicit hadith. Building a structure on the grave for adornment is haram, as it involves waste and resembles the practices of non-believers. Building for preservation (such as a dome or wall) after burial is disliked (makruh), as it conflicts with the transient nature of the grave. However, before burial, the land is not a grave so building is permissible. Some Hanafi works (al-Nawazil) allow plastering with mud (tityan) as a preservation measure, and the fatwa is upon this. Similarly, writing on a stone that marks the grave is permissible if it is needed to preserve the location, despite the hadith prohibiting writing; the Hanafi school allows it for necessity. The commentary provides a detailed discussion on the differences within the school.

Key Terms
التربيع (al-tarbi'): Making the grave square in shape rather than the musannam (humped) form.
التجصيص (al-tajsis): Plastering the grave with gypsum or lime.
البناء (al-bina): Constructing a structure (dome, wall, etc.) on the grave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When it is built before burial
B) When it is built for adornment and decoration
C) When it is built to preserve the grave from being lost
D) When it is built using mud instead of plaster

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school forbids squaring and plastering graves and building for adornment, but permits building for preservation (makruh) and writing on necessary markers, reflecting a balance between textual prohibition and practical need.

Rulings on Shaping and Decorating Graves
Rulings on grave construction from Maraqi al-Falah with Tahtawi's commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on tasnim, tarbi', tajsis, and building on graves, and apply the Prophetic prohibition to derive the hukm.

Core Idea
The Prophet forbade squaring and plastering graves; Hanafis rule them makruh tahrimi, while tasnim is sunnah.

This lesson examines the recommended shape of the grave and the prohibitions surrounding its construction and decoration. Drawing from the matn of Maraqi al-Falah and the commentary of al-Tahtawi, we will identify which practices are sunnah, which are makruh, and which are haram, and understand the dalil behind each ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the practices and their rulings
From the text, extract each practice: tasnim, adding extra soil, raising height, tarbi', tajsis, building for adornment, building for preservation, and applying clay. Note the ruling for each as stated in the matn.
The matn uses 'yusannim' (he makes camel-humped) as an instruction, indicating sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil for prohibitions
The text cites 'nahy al-nabi' (Prophetic prohibition) for tarbi' and tajsis. Identify the specific prophetic report (hadith of Jabir) and note that it also covers building and writing.
The hadith is ahad (single narration), so the ruling is zanni al-thubut, making the prohibition at the level of makruh tahrimi in Hanafi usul.
3
Apply Hanafi usul to determine hukm levels
In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates obligation unless there is a qarinah. However, 'yusannim' is seen as sunnah due to contrary evidence. A prohibition (nahy) indicates tahrim (prohibition). For tarbi' and tajsis, the nahy makes them haram, but Hanafis categorize them as makruh tahrimi because the prohibition is interpreted as makruh tanzihi? Actually, the text says 'la yurabba' wa la yujassas' with nahy, so they are prohibited. The commentary clarifies it is makruh tahrimi.
The difference between haram and makruh tahrimi is sometimes semantic; in practice, both require avoidance.
4
Note intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and preferred view
There is disagreement on the height of the grave (handspan vs four fingers) and on adding extra soil. Al-Tahtawi cites the Nawazil for permission to apply clay, which is the mufta bihi position.
The mufta bihi is: tasnim sunnah, tarbi' and tajsis makruh tahrimi, building for adornment haram, building for preservation makruh, clay application permissible.
5
Distinguish cross-madhhab differences
Shafi'is consider tarbi' as afdal because they believe the Prophet's grave was square. Hanafis and most other schools follow the hadith forbidding it. Understand the practical consequence (thamar al-khilaf) at the grave.
This difference affects the shape of graves in regions following different madhhabs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أتى القبر فحثى عليه التراب من قبل رأسه ثلاثاً (ويسنم القبر) ويكره أن يزيد فيه على التراب الذي خرج منه ويجعله مرتفعاً عن الأرض قدر شبر، أو أكثر بقليل، ولا بأس برش الماء حفظاً له ولا يربع) ولا يجصص لنهي النبي عن تربيع القبور وتجصيصها (ويحرم البناء عليه للزينة) لما روينا (ويكره) البناء عليه للأحكام بعد الدفن) لأنه للبقاء والقبر للفناء، وأما قبل الدفن فليس بقبر، وفي النوازل لا بأس بتطيينه، وفي الغيائية، وعليه الفتوى
Then he came to the grave and threw soil on it from the direction of its head three times (and he makes the grave camel-humped). It is disliked to add to it soil beyond what came out of it, and he makes it raised above the ground about a handspan, or a little more. There is no harm in sprinkling water for its preservation. And he does not make it square, and he does not plaster it, due to the Prophet's prohibition of squaring graves and plastering them. (And building upon it for adornment is forbidden) due to what we narrated. (And it is disliked) to build upon it for rulings after burial, because it is for permanence and the grave is for decay. As for before burial, it is not a grave. In al-Nawazil, there is no harm in plastering it with clay, and in al-Ghay'iyyah [؟], and upon it is the fatwa.
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement from the matn of Maraqi al-Falah followed by commentary from al-Tahtawi. It addresses the recommended method of shaping the grave after burial. The grave should be made 'musannam' (camel-humped), i.e., raised in the middle like a camel's hump, as opposed to being flat. It is disliked (makruh) to add extra soil beyond that which was excavated, and the height should be about a handspan (shibr) or slightly more. There is no harm in sprinkling water on the grave to help preserve its form. It is prohibited (haram) to make the grave square (tarbi') or to plaster it (tajsis), based on the Prophet's prohibition. Building structures on the grave for adornment is also forbidden. However, before burial, the site is not considered a grave, so building there is not disliked. In the Nawazil, it is said that there is no harm in sealing the grave with clay, and this is the relied-upon position (fatwa).

Key Terms
تسنيم (tasnim): Making the grave elevated in the middle like a camel's hump, as opposed to being flat (taswiyah).
تربيع (tarbi'): Making the grave square or building a square structure over it.
تجصيص (tajsis): Plastering the grave with gypsum or similar material.
تطيين (tatyin): Plastering the grave with clay or mud, as opposed to gypsum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Mubah
C) Makruh tahrimi (prohibited)

Key Takeaway
Tasnim is sunnah; tarbi' and tajsis are prohibited; applying clay is permissible; building intent determines ruling.

Writing on Graves: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on writing on grave markers with proof and disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on writing on grave markers, identify the intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa/Muhammad, and apply the condition of necessity that changes the ruling from makruh to permissible.

Core Idea
Writing on graves is makruh but becomes permissible when needed to preserve the grave trace.

The passage addresses a practical issue: marking graves with writing to prevent their location from being forgotten. While the Hanafi school generally discourages writing on graves, it recognizes that preserving the grave's identity may override the dislike. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the evidence from the Sunnah, and the nuanced position that balances respect for the deceased with practical need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on writing on graves
Find the explicit statement in the text: 'there is no harm in writing on a stone placed on the grave to preserve its trace.' This indicates a permissive stance under certain conditions.
Note the phrase 'لا بأس' (no harm) which implies mubah (permissible) in this context, but the default is makruh.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi disagreement
The text mentions that Abu Yusuf disliked writing on graves. Understand that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani considered it permissible when necessary, while Abu Yusuf held the stricter view.
3
Analyze the proof from the Sunnah
Two hadiths are cited: the Prophet fixing a stone on his son Ibrahim's grave (indicating permissibility of marking), and the hadith about wind and rain expiating sins (showing benefit of preserving the grave).
The hadith about the stone is from Bukhari; the wind and rain hadith is less authentic but used as supporting evidence.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
Based on al-Muhit and al-Tahtawi, the relied-upon view is that writing is permissible when needed to preserve the grave; otherwise it remains disliked. This is the dominant fatwa position.
The tarjih authority is given as al-Tahtawi citing al-Muhit.
5
Compare with other schools
Shafi'is generally forbid writing absolutely; Malikis permit it for identification only. The Hanafi position is intermediate, allowing it under necessity.
This cross-madhhab comparison highlights the Hanafi emphasis on necessity (darurah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ولا بأس أيضاً (بالكتابة) في حجر صين به القبر ووضع عليه لئلا يذهب الأثر) أفسده، فيحترم للعلم بصاحبه ولا يمتهن) وعن أبي يوسف أنه كره أن يكتب عليه وإذا خرجت القبور فلا بأس بتطيينها لأنّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مر بقبر ابنه إبراهيم فرأى فيه حجر وقال : من عمل عملاً فليتقنه وعن أنس عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: «خفق الرياح وقطر الأمطار على قبر المؤمن كفارة لذنوبه ويكره الدفن في البيوت لاختصاصه بالأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام) قال الكمال: لا يدفن صغير ولا كبير في البيت الذي مات فيه فإن ذلك خاص بالأنبياء عليهم السلام، بل يدفن في مقابر المسلمين ويكره الدفن في الأماكن التي تسمى (الفساقي) وهي كبيت معقود بالبناء يسع جماعة قياماً، ونحوه لمخالفتها السنة (ولا بأس بدفن أكثر من واحد في قبر واحد (للضرورة) قاله قاضيخان (ويحجز بين كل اثنين بالتراب) هكذا أمر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في بعض الغزوات ولو بلي الميت، وصار تراباً جاز دفن
And there is no harm also in writing on a stone that is used to protect the grave and placed upon it so that the trace does not disappear, it is damaged [؟], so it is respected for the knowledge of its owner and not dishonored. And from Abu Yusuf that he disliked writing on it. And when the graves are [؟], there is no harm in plastering them because the Messenger of Allah passed by the grave of his son Ibrahim and saw a stone in it and said: 'Whoever does a deed, let him do it skillfully.' And from Anas from the Prophet that he said: 'The shaking of winds and the falling of rain on the grave of a believer are expiation for his sins.' And it is disliked to bury in houses because it is specific to the Prophets. Al-Kamal said: No minor or major is buried in the house in which he died, for that is specific to the Prophets, rather he is buried in Muslim graveyards. And it is disliked to bury in places called al-Fasaqi, which are like a building that can hold a group standing, etc., because they contradict the Sunnah. And there is no harm in burying more than one in a single grave due to necessity, Qadikhan said. And a barrier of soil is placed between every two, as the Messenger of Allah commanded in some battles. And if the deceased has decomposed and become dust, it is permissible to bury [another].
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage continues the rulings on graves. Regarding writing on graves: The matn states there is no harm in writing on a stone marker to preserve the grave's location, provided it is done respectfully. However, Abu Yusuf disliked it. The hashiya notes a conflict with a hadith that forbids writing, but al-Muhit distinguishes: if writing is needed to preserve the grave, it is permissible; otherwise, it is disliked. Next, it is disliked to bury in houses as that is exclusively for Prophets. Burying in structures called 'fasaqi' (enclosed buildings) is also disliked as it contradicts the Sunnah. Multiple burials in one grave are permissible only for necessity, such as shortage of gravediggers or overcrowding. In such cases, a soil barrier is placed between each body, and the most virtuous is placed toward the qibla. If the first body has fully decomposed, it is permissible to bury another in the same grave.

Key Terms
لا بأس (la ba'sa): Literally 'no harm', used in fiqh to indicate permissibility (mubah or ja'iz).
فساقي (fasaqi): A type of built structure for burial, like a domed building.
ضرورة (darurah): Legal necessity that permits otherwise prohibited acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always forbidden
B) Permissible only for Prophets
C) Permissible when needed to preserve the grave, otherwise disliked
D) Always permissible

Key Takeaway
Writing on graves is generally disliked but becomes permissible when necessary to preserve the grave's identity, based on the Prophet's practice.

Burying in Houses and Fasaqi: Prohibition for Non-Prophets
Rulings on burial locations: houses and fasaqi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why burying in houses is disliked for non-Prophets, identify the ruling on fasaqi structures, and apply the principle that burial should be in Muslim cemeteries.

Core Idea
Burying in houses is reserved for Prophets; for others it is makruh tahrimi and burying in fasaqi is also disliked.

The passage addresses two burial locations: houses and artificial structures called fasaqi. Both are discouraged for the general Muslim community. The lesson explains the special status of Prophets' burials and the general rule that Muslims should be buried in communal graveyards.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on burying in houses
The text states: 'يكره الدفن في البيوت لاختصاصه بالأنبياء' (it is disliked to bury in houses because it is specific to the Prophets). Understand that this is a strong dislike (makruh tahrimi) for non-Prophets.
The phrase 'يكره' often indicates makruh tahrimi in Hanafi terminology.
2
Analyze the exception for Prophets
Al-Kamal explains that no one, young or old, is buried in the house where they died, as that privilege is exclusively for Prophets. This indicates a definitive prohibition for others.
The rationale is that burying in houses can lead to the house being treated as a shrine or cause neglect of the grave.
3
Learn the ruling on fasaqi
The text also mentions dislike of burying in places called al-fasaqi, which are building-like structures that can hold people standing. It states they contradict the Sunnah.
Fasaqi are artificial burial chambers; the Sunnah is to dig a grave (lahd) directly in the earth.
4
Apply the general rule
The preferred practice is to bury in Muslim graveyards (مقابر المسلمين), not in private houses or special structures.

And it is disliked to bury in places called al-Fasaqi, which are like a building that can hold a group standing, etc., because they contradict the Sunnah. And there is no harm in burying more than one in a single grave due to necessity, Qadikhan said. And a barrier of soil is placed between every two, as the Messenger of Allah commanded in some battles. And if the deceased has decomposed and become dust, it is permissible to bury [another].
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage continues the rulings on graves. Regarding writing on graves: The matn states there is no harm in writing on a stone marker to preserve the grave's location, provided it is done respectfully. However, Abu Yusuf disliked it. The hashiya notes a conflict with a hadith that forbids writing, but al-Muhit distinguishes: if writing is needed to preserve the grave, it is permissible; otherwise, it is disliked. Next, it is disliked to bury in houses as that is exclusively for Prophets. Burying in structures called 'fasaqi' (enclosed buildings) is also disliked as it contradicts the Sunnah. Multiple burials in one grave are permissible only for necessity, such as shortage of gravediggers or overcrowding. In such cases, a soil barrier is placed between each body, and the most virtuous is placed toward the qibla. If the first body has fully decomposed, it is permissible to bury another in the same grave.

Key Terms
فساقي (fasaqi): A built structure used for burial, like a domed chamber.
مكروه تحريما (makruh tahrimi): An act that is strongly disliked and close to haram, but not definitively forbidden.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, burying a non-Prophet in a house is:
A) Makruh tanzih
B) Makruh tahrimi
C) Mubah
D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
Burying non-Prophets in houses or fasaqi is disliked and contradicts the Sunnah; the proper place is the Muslim graveyard.

Multiple Burials in One Grave: Conditions and Necessity
Ruling on multiple burials in one grave with condition of necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that multiple burials in one grave are only permissible due to necessity (darurah), explain the requirement of a soil barrier between bodies, and compare the order of precedence when burying multiple bodies.

Core Idea
Multiple burials in one grave are haram without necessity; with darurah, they are permissible with a soil barrier.

The passage permits burying more than one person in a single grave, but only when there is a genuine necessity, such as a shortage of gravediggers or space. It also prescribes a soil barrier between each body, following the Prophet's command in a battle. This lesson explains the conditions and the order of placement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling on multiple burials
The text says 'لا بأس بدفن أكثر من واحد في قبر واحد للضرورة' (no harm in burying more than one in a single grave due to necessity). This implies that without necessity, it is forbidden (haram).
The default is that each person has their own grave; multiple burials are an exception.
2
Understand the condition of darurah
Necessity (darurah) is what permits the otherwise forbidden act. Examples include lack of cemetery space, shortage of gravediggers, or emergency situations.
The necessity must be genuine, not just convenience.
3
Learn the requirement of a soil barrier
The text commands: 'ويحجز بين كل اثنين بالتراب' (a barrier of soil is placed between every two). This is a condition for validity.
The soil barrier prevents the bodies from touching each other, as it may be disrespectful.
4
Apply the order of precedence
Although not explicit in this passage, Hanafi fiqh specifies that when multiple bodies are buried in one grave, the most virtuous is placed towards the qibla, then the next, etc. The order: first adult men, then boys, then khuntha (hermaphrodites), then women.
This order is derived from other Hanafi sources and is part of the complete ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ولا بأس أيضاً (بالكتابة) في حجر صين به القبر ووضع عليه لئلا يذهب الأثر) أفسده، فيحترم للعلم بصاحبه ولا يمتهن) وعن أبي يوسف أنه كره أن يكتب عليه وإذا خرجت القبور فلا بأس بتطيينها لأنّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مر بقبر ابنه إبراهيم فرأى فيه حجر وقال : من عمل عملاً فليتقنه وعن أنس عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: «خفق الرياح وقطر الأمطار على قبر المؤمن كفارة لذنوبه ويكره الدفن في البيوت لاختصاصه بالأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام) قال الكمال: لا يدفن صغير ولا كبير في البيت الذي مات فيه فإن ذلك خاص بالأنبياء عليهم السلام، بل يدفن في مقابر المسلمين ويكره الدفن في الأماكن التي تسمى (الفساقي) وهي كبيت معقود بالبناء يسع جماعة قياماً، ونحوه لمخالفتها السنة (ولا بأس بدفن أكثر من واحد في قبر واحد (للضرورة) قاله قاضيخان (ويحجز بين كل اثنين بالتراب) هكذا أمر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في بعض الغزوات ولو بلي الميت، وصار تراباً جاز دفن
And there is no harm also in writing on a stone that is used to protect the grave and placed upon it so that the trace does not disappear, it is damaged [؟], so it is respected for the knowledge of its owner and not dishonored. And from Abu Yusuf that he disliked writing on it. And when the graves are [؟], there is no harm in plastering them because the Messenger of Allah passed by the grave of his son Ibrahim and saw a stone in it and said: 'Whoever does a deed, let him do it skillfully.' And from Anas from the Prophet that he said: 'The shaking of winds and the falling of rain on the grave of a believer are expiation for his sins.' And it is disliked to bury in houses because it is specific to the Prophets. Al-Kamal said: No minor or major is buried in the house in which he died, for that is specific to the Prophets, rather he is buried in Muslim graveyards. And it is disliked to bury in places called al-Fasaqi, which are like a building that can hold a group standing, etc., because they contradict the Sunnah. And there is no harm in burying more than one in a single grave due to necessity, Qadikhan said. Transporting the Deceased and Exhumation Rulings
Rulings on transferring and exhuming the deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on transporting a deceased beyond two miles and identify the conditions under which exhumation is permissible.

Core Idea
After burial, exhumation is absolutely prohibited except for valid legal rights like returning usurped land.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rulings on moving a deceased person before and after burial, and the strict prohibition of exhumation once the grave is sealed. Through a careful reading of the text, you will learn the default rulings, the exceptional cases where exhumation is allowed, and the weight of the evidence (dalil) that supports these positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on transport distance
The text states that transporting a deceased up to two miles is not blameworthy, but beyond that is disliked (makruh). Note the distinction: before burial, transport is generally permissible; after burial, it becomes restricted.
This ruling is based on practice (Ya'qub and Sa'd) but qualified by concern for putrefaction.
2
Recognize the prohibition of exhumation
After the soil is poured (ihālat al-turāb), exhumation is absolutely forbidden by consensus of the Hanafi imams, regardless of duration.
The prohibition is a right of Allah (haqq Allah).
3
Analyze the exceptions
Two exceptions: (1) if the land is usurped, the owner may demand removal; (2) if the land is taken by pre-emption (shuf'ah), the pre-emptor may require removal. These are legal rights that override the prohibition.
Also consider the guarantee for digging if buried in another's grave.
4
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The text cites the transport of Ya'qub (from Egypt to Syria) and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas (4 leagues to Medina) as proof of permissibility for transport. However, the dislike is reconciled by the exceptional holiness of these individuals, meaning the general rule remains dislike.
These are ahad reports, giving zanni certainty.
5
Evaluate the dispute on maternal grief
Some later Hanafi jurists allowed exhumation for a mother who cannot bear separation. The text rejects this view as not relied upon, affirming the absolute prohibition. The Thamarah al-Khilaf: a mother following the dominant view cannot exhume.
Tarjih: the prohibition is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(أو ميلين) ونحو ذلك لا بأس به لأن المسافة إلى المقابر قد تبلغ هذا المقدار (وكره نقله لأكثر منه أي أكثر من الميلين كذا في الظهيرية، وقال شمس الأئمة السرخسي : وقول محمد في الكتاب لا بأس أن ينقل الميت قدر ميل أو ميلين بيان أن النقل من بلد إلى بلد مكروه قاله قاضيخان وقد قال قبله لو مات في غير بلده يستحب تركه فإن نقل إلى مصر آخر لا بأس به لما روي أنّ يعقوب صلوات الله عليه مات بمصر، ونقل إلى الشام وسعد بن أبي وقاص مات في ضيعة على أربعة فراسخ المدينة ونقل على أعناق الرجال إلى المدينة قلت : يمكن الجمع بأن الزيادة مكروهة في تغير الرائحة، أو خشيتها وتنتفي بانتفائها لمن هو مثل يعقوب عليه السلام أو سعد رضي الله عنه لأنهما من احياء الدارين (ولا يجوز نقله) أي الميت بعد دفنه بأن أهيل عليه التراب، وأما قبله فيخرج (بالإجماع) بين أئمتنا طالت مدة دفنه أو قصرت للنهي عن نبشه والنبش حرام حقاً الله تعالى (إلا أن تكون الأرض مغصوبة) فيخرج لحق صاحبها إن طلبه وإن شاء سواه بالأرض، وانتفع بها زراعة، أو غيرها (أو أخذت الأرض (بالشفعة) بأن دفن فيها بعد الشراء ثم أخذت بالشفعة لحق الشفيع فيتخير كما قلنا وإن دفن في قبر حفر لغيره من الأحياء بأرض ليست مملوكة لأحد (ضمن قيمة الحفر) من تركته وإلا فمن بيت المال أو المسلمين كما قدمناه فإن كانت المقبرة واسعة يكره ذلك لأن صاحب القبر يستوحش بذلك، وإن كانت الأرض ضيقة جاز أي بلا كراهة قال الفقيه أبو الليث رحمه الله : لأن أحداً من الناس لا يدري بأي أرض يموت، وهذا كمن بسط بساطاً، أو مصلى أي سجادة في المسجد أو المجلس فإن كان المكان واسعاً لا يصلي ولا يجلس عليه غيره وإن كان المكان ضيقاً جاز لغيره أن يرفع البساط، ويصلي في ذلك المكان أو يجلس ومن حفر قبراً لنفسه قبل موته، فلا بأس به ويؤجر عليه هكذا عمل عمر بن عبد العزيز والربيع بن خثعم وغيرهما (ولا يخرج منه) لا تصبر وأرادت نبشه ونقله إلى بلدها لا يباح لها ذلك فتجويز بعض المتأخرين لا يلتفت إليه، ولا يباح نبشه بعد الدفن أصلاً كذا في الفتح وغيره.
(Or two miles) and the like, it is not problematic because the distance to cemeteries may reach this amount. (And it is disliked to transport him more than that) meaning more than two miles—thus in al-Zahiriyyah. And Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: Muhammad's statement in the book 'there is no harm in transporting the deceased a mile or two' indicates that transporting from a town to a town is disliked—Qadikhan said this. And he said before: if one dies outside his town, it is recommended to leave him; if he is transported to another Egypt, there is no harm due to the report that Ya'qub (peace be upon him) died in Egypt and was transported to Syria, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas died in a village four leagues from Medina and was transported on the shoulders of men to Medina. I say: it is possible to reconcile that the increase is disliked due to concern about change of smell, and that concern is absent for someone like Ya'qub or Sa'd because they are among the living of the two abodes. (And it is not permissible to transport him) i.e., the deceased after burial, meaning after soil has been poured over him. As for before that, he is taken out (by consensus) among our imams, whether the duration of his burial was long or short, due to the prohibition of exhuming him; exhumation is unlawful as a right of Allah (except if the land is usurped), so he is taken out for the right of its owner if he requests it, and if he wishes he may leave him in the land and benefit from it by cultivation or other purposes. (Or if the land is taken by pre-emption) by burying in it after purchase, then it is taken by pre-emption—the pre-emptor has the right to choose as we said. And if he is buried in a grave dug for another living person in land not owned by anyone, (the value of the digging is guaranteed) from his estate, otherwise from the treasury or from the Muslims as we explained. If the cemetery is spacious, that is disliked because the grave's owner feels lonely by it; if the land is cramped, it is permissible without dislike. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: because no one knows in which land he will die, and this is like one who spreads a mat or prayer rug in a mosque or gathering: if the place is spacious, no one else may pray or sit on it; if the place is cramped, it is permissible for another to move the mat and pray or sit there. And whoever digs a grave for himself before death, there is no harm and he will be rewarded for it—such was the practice of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz, al-Rabi' ibn Khuthaym, and others. (And he is not taken out from it). If a mother cannot bear it and wants to exhume him and transport him to her town, it is not permissible for her. The permission of some later jurists is not relied upon. Exhumation after burial is not allowed at all—thus in al-Fath and others.
Source pages p. 614

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah on Maraqi al-Falah refines rulings on transporting a deceased person and exhuming graves. It begins by stating that transporting a body up to two miles is permissible because cemeteries may be that far. Transporting beyond two miles is makruh (disliked). The author cites Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi who explains that Imam Muhammad's statement in the original text indicates a blanket dislike for transporting from one town to another. However, there are exceptions: the prophets Ya'qub (transported from Egypt to Syria) and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas (transported four leagues to Medina) are cited as evidence that for special persons it is allowed. The commentator reconciles that the dislike is due to fear of putrefaction, which does not apply to such saintly individuals. After burial (once soil is poured), exhumation is unanimously prohibited among Hanafis, whether the burial was short or long, because it is a violation of the grave which is a right of Allah. Exceptions are made when the land is usurped—the rightful owner may demand exhumation and removal of the body. Similarly, if land is taken by pre-emption (shuf'ah), the pre-emptor may require removal. If someone is buried in a grave dug for another living person in non-owned land, the digger's heirs or the treasury must compensate for the digging. In a spacious cemetery, this is disliked because it disturbs the original grave's owner; in cramped conditions, it is permissible. The commentator analogizes to someone spreading a mat in a mosque: in a spacious area, others may not move it; in tight quarters, they may. Digging one's own grave before death is commendable, as practiced by early Muslims. Finally, it is emphatically stated that once buried, a body cannot be exhumed even for a mother's grief; contrary views of some later scholars are dismissed.

Key Terms
نبش (nabsh): Exhumation of a deceased person from the grave after burial.
إهالة التراب (ihālat al-turāb): Pouring soil over the deceased in the grave, marking the completion of burial.
شفعة (shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption in property; if land is taken by shuf'ah after burial, the pre-emptor may require exhumation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the deceased's mother cannot bear the separation.
B) When the land is usurped and the owner demands removal.
C) When the body needs to be moved to a family plot.
D) When the cemetery is being relocated for public works.

Key Takeaway
Transporting a deceased beyond two miles is makruh, and exhumation after burial is haram except for overriding legal rights like usurped land or pre-emption.

When Is Exhumation Permitted? Property vs. Positioning
Exhumation rulings for property vs. positioning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when exhumation is permitted and when it is prohibited, and explain the rationale using the distinction between property rights and post-burial inviolability.

Core Idea
Property rights justify exhumation; mere misplacement does not.

This lesson from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya clarifies the boundaries of permissible exhumation. While the grave is generally inviolable, the Hanafi school carves out exceptions for retrieving lost property or a usurped shroud, based on Prophetic precedent. However, correcting the deceased's positioning (non-qibla direction, left side, head-feet reversal) does not warrant such disturbance. The passage also notes a variant opinion advocating side-tunneling to avoid full exposure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and scenarios
The act under discussion is exhumation (nabsh al-qabr). The passage lists three scenarios: (1) a lost item (garment, coin) fell into the grave; (2) a usurped shroud placed on the deceased; (3) the body is mispositioned. For each, note the ruling.
Scenario (1) and (2) are property-related; scenario (3) is about positioning.
2
Determine the hukm for each scenario
For scenarios (1) and (2), exhumation is permissible (ja'iz) — and becomes obligatory if the property owner insists. For scenario (3), exhumation is not permitted. The text says 'لا ينبش' (it is not dug up). A partial exception: if only bricks were placed and earth not poured, bricks are removed to correct positioning.
The reasoning: property rights override the grave's inviolability; but a mere error in positioning does not justify disturbance.
3
Examine the dalil for property cases
The proof cited is the Prophet's (ﷺ) permission to dig up the grave of Abu Righal to retrieve a gold rod. This shows a precedent for retrieving property from a grave. The dalil is ahad (single narration) and thus zanni al-thubut, but sufficient for permissibility.
The Hanafi school accepts such ahad hadith in non-essential matters.
4
Consider the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on method
Some Hanafi scholars (the 'قيل' in the text) say the grave should not be fully dug up; instead, a tunnel should be dug from the side to reach the item, avoiding exposure of the body. This alternative respects both property rights and the deceased's dignity.
Both views are considered legitimate; the mufta bihi (operative fatwa) permits full exhumation if necessary.
5
Apply the ruling to the positioning scenario
If the body is placed incorrectly (not facing qibla, on left side, head at feet), exhumation is not allowed. Instead, if bricks have been laid but earth not yet poured, the bricks are removed and the sunna positioning is implemented without full exhumation. This respects the body after burial.
This is a critical refinement: the prohibition is only after earth has been poured; before that, adjustment is possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينبش القبر (المتاع) كثوب ودرهم (سقط فيه) وقيل : لا ينبش، بل يحفر من جهة المتاع ويخرج (و) ينبش الكفن مغصوب) لم يرض صاحبه إلا يأخذه (ومال) مع الميت لأن النبي أباح نبش قبر أبي رغال لذلك (ولا ينبش) الميت (بوضعه لغير القبلة أو وضعه على يساره أو جعل رأسه موضع رجليه، ولو سوي اللبن عليه ولم يهل التراب نزع اللبن وراعي السنة.
The grave is dug up for an item (like a garment or dirham) that fell into it. Some say: it is not dug up; rather, one digs from the side of the item and removes it. And the shroud that was usurped is dug up if its owner does not agree except to take it. And property placed with the deceased, because the Prophet permitted digging up the grave of Abu Righal for that reason. And the deceased is not dug up if placed facing other than the qibla, or placed on his left side, or his head placed where his feet should be. If the bricks were placed on him and earth was not poured, the bricks are removed and the sunna is observed.
Source pages p. 616

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's hashya on Maraqi al-Falah addresses cases where exhumation is required, permitted, or forbidden. The ruling: If a belonging of the living (like a garment or coin) falls into the grave and cannot be retrieved without digging, the grave is dug up to retrieve it. Some scholars say it is better to dig from the side without exposing the body. If the shroud is usurped (ghasb) and its owner demands it back, the grave is dug up to return it. Similarly, if property (like money) was buried with the deceased for preservation, exhumation is allowed based on the precedent of the Prophet allowing the grave of Abu Righal to be dug for a gold rod. However, if the body was placed incorrectly (not facing qibla, on its left side, or head at feet), it is not exhumed just to correct the position; rather, if bricks were laid but no earth poured, the bricks are removed and the proper sunna is followed. The hukm for exhumation in these cases is ja'iz (permissible) except where it is obligatory when the item's owner insists. The authority weight is from the later muta'akhkhirin (fatawa) as al-Tahtawi is a later commentator.

Key Terms
نبش القبر (nabsh al-qabr): Digging up the grave to remove something or the body.
كفن مغصوب (kafan maghsub): A shroud taken without permission (usurped) placed on the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is exhumation for a lost item permitted?
A) Because the deceased does not own the item any longer
B) Because property rights are given priority over grave inviolability
C) Because the Prophet explicitly commanded it for all cases
D) Because it is a sunna to dig up graves for any reason

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ownership rights justify exhumation, but mere mispositioning after burial does not.

Post-Burial Etiquette and Disliked Practices
Recommendations after burial and prohibitions on gatherings and hospitality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which post-burial practices are makruh and explain the evidence and scholarly differences.

Core Idea
Post-burial gatherings and hospitality by the family are disliked, but limited practices without prohibited elements are allowed.

After burial, the family and community have certain etiquettes. This lesson examines two specific practices: sitting at the door for mourning and the family hosting meals for visitors. While the later Hanafi masters declare both makruh, a careful reading of the hadith evidence reveals nuance and exceptions. Understanding these rulings protects against both unnecessary hardship and innovation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The passage rules on two acts: sitting at the door for mourning and the family hosting meals. Both are initially stated as makruh (disliked). Note the source of the ruling.
Dislike may be tahrimi (close to haram) due to resemblance to Jahiliyyah.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The primary dalil for the dislike of hosting meals is the hadith of Jarir ibn Abdullah: 'We used to consider gathering at the family’s home and their preparing food as part of wailing.'
This hadith is found in Ahmad and Ibn Majah with a sound chain.
3
Examine the counter-evidence
A second hadith (from an Ansari) shows the Prophet eating a meal prepared by the deceased’s family, indicating permissibility. This creates a conflict that must be resolved.
Al-Burhan al-Halabi uses this to question the strict dislike.
4
Understand the tarjih and exceptions
The later Hanafi position weighs the evidence: the dislike applies when the gathering involves prohibited acts (e.g., spreading mats, excessive food). If done modestly for the poor, it becomes good (hasan). Sitting at the door for up to three days without prohibited acts is not blameworthy.
Al-Bazzaziyya states that making food for the poor is good; al-Burhan al-Halabi notes no clear evidence for strict dislike.

تتمة : قال كثير من متأخري أئتمنا رحمهم الله : يكره الاجتماع عند صاحب الميت حتى يأتي إليه من يعزي بل إذا رجع الناس من الدفن فليتفرقوا، ويشتغلوا بأمورهم وصاحب الميت بأمره ويكره الجلوس على باب الدار للمصيبة فإنّ ذلك عمل أهل الجاهلية، ونهى النبي عن ذلك، وتكره في المسجد وتكره الضيافة من أهل الميت لأنها شرعت في يسير . هكذا الخ، وقيل: يلهمه الله تعالى فيجيب كما ألهم عيسى عليه السلام في المهد، وحكمة السؤال إظهار شرف المؤمن وخذلان الكافر، واستثنى بعض أكابر أهل السنة جماعة، فلا يسألون منهم المقتول في ركة الكفار والمرابط والمطعون ومن مات في زمن الطاعون والمبطون والمجنون وأهل الفترة والميت ليلة الجمعة ويومها والقارىء كل ليلة سورة الملك، وطالب العلم لقوله : من جاء أجله وهو يطلب العلم لقي الله ولم يكن بينه وبين النبيين إلا درجة النبوة كذا في جواهر الكلام والحديث رواه الطبراني والدارمي وابن السني بلفظ من جاءه ملك الموت، وهو يطلب العلم ليحيي به الإسلام فبينه وبين النبوة درجة واحدة في الجنة كما في تخريج الأحياء والمقاصد الحسنة، وفي المبتغى بالغين اتباع جنازة الغريب، أو الجار الصالح أفضل من النوافل وإلا فهي أفضل ا هـ، وفي شرعة الإسلام، والسنة أن يتصدق ولي الميت له قبل مضي الليلة الأولى بشيء مما تيسر له فإن لم يجد شيئاً فليصل ركعتين، ثم يهد ثوابهما له قال، ويستحب أن يتصدق على الميت بعد الدفن إلى سبعة أيام كل يوم بشيء مما اه. قوله : ( ويكره الجلوس على باب الدار قال في شرح السيد: ولا بأس بالجلوس لها إلى ثلاثة أيام من غير ارتكاب محظور من فرش البسط، والأطعمة من أهل الميت ا هـ فإن حمل قول المصنف، ويكره الجلوس الخ على ما إذا كان بمحظور ارتفعت المخالفة، ويدل عليه ما في النهر عن التجنيس لا بأس بالجلوس لها ثلاثة أيام وكونه على باب الدار مع فرش بسط على قوارع الطريق من أقبح القبائح. قوله : ( وتكره في المسجد) قال في الدرر : لا بأس بالجلوس لها في غير مسجد ثلاثة أيام. قوله وتكره الضيافة من أهل الميت) قال في البزازية : يكره اتخاذ الطعام في اليوم الأول والثالث، وبعد الأسبوع، ونقل الطعام إلى المقبرة في المواسم واتخاذ الدعوة بقراءة القرآن وجمع الصلحاء والقراء للختم، أو لقراءة سورة الأنعام أو الإخلاص اهـ قال البرهان الحلبي : ولا يخلو عن نظر لأنه لا دليل على الكراهة إلا حديث جرير المتقدم وهو ما رواه الإمام أحمد وابن ماجه بإسناد صحيح عن جرير بن عبد الله : كنا نعد الاجتماع إلى أهل الميت وصنعهم الطعام من النياحة ا هـ يعني وهو فعل الجاهلية إنما يدل على كراهة ذلك عند الموت فقط على أنه قد عارضه ما رواه الإمام أحمد أيضاً بسند صحيح، وأبو داود عن عاصم بن كليب عن أبيه عن رجل من الأنصار قال : خرجنا مع رسول الله له في جنازة فلما رجع استقبله داعي امرأته فجاء وجيء بالطعام فوضع يده، ووضع القوم فأكلوا ورسول الله له ويلوك اللقمة في فيه الحديث فهذا يدل على إباحة صنع أهل الميت الطعام والدعوة إليه بل ذكر في البزازية أيضاً من كتاب الاستحسان، وإن اتخذ طعاماً للفقراء كان حسناً ا هـ وفي استحسان الخانية، وإن اتخذو لي الميت طعاماً للفقراء كان
Appendix: Many of our later imams, may Allah have mercy on them, said: It is disliked to gather at the home of the deceased's family until the one offering condolences comes. Rather, when people return from the burial, they should disperse and attend to their affairs, and the family of the deceased to their own. And sitting at the door of the house for mourning is disliked because it is the practice of the people of ignorance, and the Prophet forbade that. And it is disliked in the mosque, and hospitality from the family of the deceased is disliked because it was prescribed in [some other context]. ... And the wisdom of the questioning is to show the honor of the believer and the humiliation of the disbeliever. Some senior Ahl al-Sunnah excluded a group who are not questioned: the one killed in the midst of disbelievers, the sentinel, the one stricken with plague, the one who died in a time of pestilence, the one with dropsy, the insane, the people of the interval, the one who dies on Friday night or day, the one who recites Surah al-Mulk every night, and the seeker of knowledge... [The author then discusses the dislike of sitting at the door, in the mosque, and hosting meals, with qualifications from other scholars.]
Source pages p. 616

Commentary
This appendix (tatimma) from al-Tahtawi collects rulings on post-burial etiquette. It begins by stating that gathering at the deceased's home for condolences before the comforter arrives is makruh (disliked). People should disperse after burial. Sitting at the door for mourning is makruh because it resembles Jahiliyyah. Sitting in the mosque for mourning is also makruh. However, some scholars like al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani qualify that sitting for up to three days without prohibited acts (like spreading mats or serving food) is not blameworthy. Hosting meals by the family (making food for visitors) is makruh according to al-Bazzaziyya, especially on specific days (first, third, after a week), and taking food to the grave is disliked. But al-Burhan al-Halabi questions this, citing a hadith where the Prophet ate at a funeral meal, indicating permissibility. The passage concludes that making food for the poor is good (hasan). The discussion also includes exceptions to the questioning in the grave (talqin) for certain persons. The overall ruling: the disliked practices are for specific scenarios; without prohibited elements, they become permissible. The Hanafi position generally discourages exaggerated mourning customs.

Key Terms
الضيافة من أهل الميت (al-diyafah min ahl al-mayyit): The family of the deceased preparing food for visitors.
الجلوس على باب الدار (al-julus 'ala bab al-dar): Sitting at the doorstep for mourning

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the family of the deceased hosting a meal for visitors?
A) Sunnah
B) Makruh
C) Haram
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Post-burial hospitality is generally makruh in the Hanafi school, but the ruling is flexible based on intention and avoidance of excess.
